Yu Xuezhong Departs Beijing by Air for Shaanxi, Transfers to Lanzhou to Assume New Post

(Nanjing) Yu Xuezhong, having completed his affairs in Beijing, departed Beijing at 12:30 PM on the 5th, accompanied by his secretary and entourage, by Boeing aircraft for Shaanxi, and will transfer to Lanzhou to assume his new post. Shao Lizi, Wang Shuchang, Hui Kuoqing, and several dozen others went to the airport to see him off. Yu told reporters before his departure that after arriving in Xi'an, he would visit Deputy Commander Zhang to seek instructions, and then proceed to Tianshui to inspect the troops, staying for about a few days before going to Lanzhou to take office. As for the policies for governing Gansu, he said that since he had transferred from his position in Hebei, he would focus solely on military affairs and was not familiar with the situation in Gansu province. He would be able to make decisions only after arriving in Gansu. Fortunately, former Chairman Zhu had achieved remarkable results in his administration, and he would strive to follow his example and seek benefits for the poor people of the Northwest. The banditry situation in Gansu Province was not severe, making it easier to suppress, and so on. (Central News Agency dispatch, 5th)

First Plenary Session Held, Anniversary of the Zhaoye Warship Uprising Commemorated

Various agencies and organizations in different locations also held commemorative meetings separately.

(Nanjing) The First Plenary Session held the 20th anniversary commemoration of the Zhaoye Warship Uprising at the Central Auditorium at 9:00 AM on the 5th. More than one hundred members of the Central Executive and Supervisory Committees attended, arranged in order according to age. After the music was played and the meeting commenced, Chairman Chen Guofu led the attendees in performing the ritual, observing three minutes of silence. Chen then delivered a detailed report on the events of the Zhaoye Uprising, which lasted for over forty minutes before the ceremony concluded. (Central News Agency dispatch, 5th)

(Nanjing) Chen Guofu, on the 5th, at the commemoration of the Zhaoye Uprising held at the Plenary Session, gave a report outlining that the overthrow of Yuan Shikai was attributed to the Zhaoye Uprising, just as the overthrow of the Manchu Qing dynasty during the Xinhai Revolution was attributed to the Huanghuagang Uprising, both sharing the same spirit. After the Second Revolution, the spirit of the Party was scattered, and command was inconsistent. Mr. Chen Yingshi sensed at that time that the revolution had failed because the comrades did not listen to the Premier. Therefore, in February of the fourth year, he returned to Shanghai, vowing to work hard in Shanghai to revive the spirit of the Party in order to overthrow Yuan's imperial dream. He first gathered comrades to work diligently in the navy, and then promoted it to the army. The uprising began to be launched in December of that year. (Describing the process of Mr. Chen Yingshi commanding the Zhaoye Uprising) Although this uprising failed due to some people not proceeding as planned, the spirit was very good, and the revolutionary force was able to manifest in Shanghai, where Yuan's defenses were tightest, shaking the entire country and eventually leading to the Yunnan Uprising, which overthrew Yuan. This is most worthy of our commemoration. We see the revolutionary spirit of Mr. Yingshi in this uprising and the bravery of the comrades involved, proving that obedience to the Premier's orders can strengthen the Party and overthrow all enemies. It is also affirmed that if comrades can obey the leader and maintain unified action, then the Party's command will be unified and the revolutionary spirit will be vibrant. Therefore, the Zhaoye Uprising holds great merit in the history of our Party. (Central News Agency dispatch, 5th)

(Anqing) All sectors of Wan gathered at the Provincial Party Headquarters at 9:00 AM on the 5th to hold a grand meeting commemorating the 20th anniversary of the Zhaoye Warship Uprising, chaired by Xu Jingzi of the Provincial Party Affairs Committee, with Wei Shouyong delivering a report. (Special dispatch, 5th)

Current Commentary

The Incident of the Tianjin Dagongbao Being Detained

— Dao

On the 3rd of this month, Tianjin Dagongbao published an article urging Song Zheyuan, no matter what, not to incite the division of the country. The entire article was tactful and well-rounded. The first paragraph expressed deep sympathy for Song's difficult situation. Then, fearing that the authorities might be misguided for a moment, it proposed two principles: (1) "At this critical juncture, it should be recognized that, no matter what, the unity of the country must be guaranteed. For public or private interests, for the country or for the region, this last line must be defended. If it is said that foreign affairs cannot be handled without dividing the country, I fear there is no such logic in the world." (2) If the country must be divided, then "the authorities must publicly take responsibility in their own names and must not use public opinion as an excuse." Finally, the newspaper believed that "for the sake of Commander Song and his staff, they should earnestly explain to Japan the necessity of maintaining China's unity, and persuade them not to go to extremes. On the one hand, they should explain the reality of the precarious environment to the government, and independently decide on a method that adapts to the current situation." However, according to yesterday's report, after this article was published, the newspaper has been ordered by the Tianjin Garrison Command since the 4th to be suspended from distribution.

Looking at this article as a whole, it takes the nation and the country as the premise throughout. The wording is also peaceful, fair, and moderate. It is tactful and indirect. Now it has been detained by the Pingjin Garrison Command, which is really puzzling. In the Pingjin area, the absurd leaflets promoting autonomy issued by Chinese traitors are everywhere. The local garrison command can watch with folded arms and not interfere. Why can it not tolerate this text urging the North China authorities to pay attention to national unity? Moreover, this article in Dagongbao is purely advisory in nature. Its motive is nothing more than fearing that the authorities are confused and trapped in fallacies, so it specifically suggests from the sidelines. The content does not specify that the North China authorities have any suspicions, which is very different from simple slander. Furthermore, the North China authorities can regard this kind of text as "correcting it if there is something wrong, and adding encouragement if there is nothing wrong." If they truly stand on the position of representing the interests of the nation and the country, then their actions will eventually be made clear to the people of the country and will be understood by the people of the country. There is really no need to take such unwise measures.

We cannot help but deeply feel the importance of eliminating interference in the field of speech here. As the country is in a time of serious crisis, if the government wants to respond firmly and effectively, it should first allow the great voice of the field of speech to exert its due authority, so that traitors will be afraid and those who plot rebellion will have nothing to borrow. And to arouse the national consciousness and national concept of the people of the whole country. If we do not pay attention to this point, the future of the country is really deeply worrying.

According to the latest news, the Dagongbao detention incident has been ordered to be released by the Ministry of Transportation. This unfortunate problem is expected to be resolved. We only hope that similar incidents will not happen again in the future.

British and French Experts Draft a Peace Agreement, Also Submitted to Italy, Much Land Swapped Between Italy and Abyssinia

(Paris) According to reliable sources, the new peace plan drafted by British and French experts was completed today and will be forwarded to the Italian government by the Italian Ambassador to France, Cerutti. The contents of the plan are as follows:

(1) Italy cedes the Port of Assab and a strip of land in Eritrea to Abyssinia, and Abyssinia builds a railway in the area, with funding provided by the League of Nations.

(2) The border of Eritrea is revised to cede part of the Tigre province to Italy, but Aksum and Adwa must be returned to Abyssinia.

(3) The border of Italian Somaliland is revised to cede part of the Ogaden province, south of 8 degrees north latitude, to Italy.

(4) The remaining land of Abyssinia remains independent and does not need to be placed under international co-management as suggested by the Committee of Five, but the Abyssinian Emperor may conclude an assistance treaty with the League of Nations. French officials believe that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will be able to accept this suggestion, and hope that Mussolini can consider this the final concession. The French side solemnly declares that the exchange of land between the two sides is a completely autonomous action. The plan was drafted on a broad basis, and there are still differences between the opinions of the United Kingdom and France, which can be revised during negotiations in Rome. (国民电, 4th)

(Paris) After consultations, British and French experts have submitted a new proposal to Italy to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian War as soon as possible. According to informed sources, the United Kingdom and France believe that this proposal can serve as the basis for resolving the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. It was delivered to the Italian Ambassador to Paris, Cerutti, by French Prime Minister Laval yesterday afternoon. The purpose of this move is clearly to elicit some opinions from Mussolini, so that when British Foreign Secretary Hoare and Laval meet on the 6th, there will be something to base it on. However, Italy seems unlikely to give a satisfactory reply. Although Laval has stated emphatically that this is the last proposal that can be put forward before the Eighteenth Committee meets to consider the oil embargo, according to dispatches from Rome, it is difficult to hope that Mussolini will accept it. It is widely believed that this proposal was formulated following the guidelines of previous talks, and contains the idea of ​​broadening the country by ceding the Port of Assab in southeastern Eritrea, along with a corner of land, to Abyssinia. A railway can be built on this land to connect the Abyssinian capital to Assab, and will be supervised by the League of Nations. Italy will also return the holy city of Aksum and Adwa to Abyssinia. Abyssinia will cede the entire southern Ogaden province to Italy, and allow for important revisions to be made to the borders of the Tigre and Harar provinces. The Committee of Fifteen also suggested previously that many economic benefits of the Abyssinian homeland be given to Italy, which is now being mentioned again. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

(London) The Italian Ambassador to the United Kingdom, Grandi, met with Foreign Office Undersecretary Vansittart today, and the Italian Ambassador to France, Cerutti, also held talks with French Prime Minister Laval. People here attach great importance to these two matters. It is rumored that Cerutti presented an important document to Laval on behalf of Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 4th)

(Geneva) Dispatches from London and Rome have been received here stating that the Italo-Abyssinian issue is currently being negotiated by the governments of the United Kingdom, France, and Italy in order to seek a peaceful resolution. Officials in charge of the League of Nations believe that the attitudes of all parties have indeed softened in the recent negotiations, but due to a lack of accurate information, it is difficult to predict what the future of the talks will be. As of now, the Eighteenth Committee is still scheduled to meet on December 11th to discuss the oil embargo issue. The postponement of the meeting has not been considered. However, if the negotiations have materialized and the basis for a peace agreement has been accepted by both Italy and Abyssinia before December 12th, then the Eighteenth Committee may postpone the meeting. If so, a special meeting of the League of Nations Administrative Council will be convened immediately, and the draft Italo-Abyssinian peace agreement will be submitted to the Committee of Five for review. This Committee of Five to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute has not yet been dissolved. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 4th)

Appointment of Hoare and Mussolini to Meet is Uncertain, British and French Foreign Ministers Will Meet in Paris

(London) According to reliable sources, Foreign Secretary Hoare will go to Switzerland to recuperate this time, and will stop in Paris on the way to meet with French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval. Around Christmas or New Year's, he will meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Switzerland. It is said that Mussolini has only left the country three times since taking power. The first time was in December 1922 to attend the London Conference to discuss the German reparations issue. The conference had no results, and France then took the action of sending troops to occupy the Ruhr region. The second time was in 1923, to go to Lausanne, Switzerland, to participate in the Turkish-Greek peace conference and conclude the Treaty of Lausanne. The third time was in 1925, to go to Locarno, Switzerland, to conclude the Locarno Pact. If he goes to Switzerland to meet with the British Foreign Secretary this time, it will be the fourth time he has left the country. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 5th)

(London) Officials have now denied the claim that Foreign Secretary Hoare will meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Switzerland. Hoare, along with his wife and one private secretary, is expected to fly to Paris tomorrow afternoon to meet with French Prime Minister Laval. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 5th)

(London) There are still many differences in opinion between the United Kingdom and France, and further discussions will be held at the end of this week when Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval meet in Paris. The United Kingdom agrees to demarcate the city of Adua and the Agam region in northern Abyssinia to Italy, or to make appropriate modifications to the boundary line between the Donakil region of Abyssinia and Italian Eritrea. As for the southern Ogaden region, which is a barren and sandy area, it can also be incorporated into Italian Somaliland. The boundary line of the proposed Italian colonization zone is: (1) The eastern boundary is the existing boundary between the Ogaden region and British Somaliland, that is, east to the Entoto Gefu area; (2) The western boundary is a straight line from Lake Chana to British Kenya. Within the aforementioned boundary line, Italy may relocate people to engage in cultivation, conduct commerce, and promote the political sovereignty of the region, which should still be retained by the Abyssinian Emperor. As for Italy, it should demarcate a road in Eritrea that leads to the Red Sea, along with the Port of Assab, and grant it to Abyssinia as an exchange. In France, it is advocated that the entire Tigre province, that is, the area currently occupied by the Italian army, be demarcated to Italy, and the boundary line between the Donakil region and Eritrea should also be given more important modifications. The southern Ogaden region should also be ceded to Italy. As for the boundary line of the colonization zone allowed to Italy, the French opinion is the same as that of the United Kingdom, but it is believed that although the political sovereignty of the region still belongs to the Abyssinian Emperor, its administrative power should be exercised by Italy, and Italy should appoint a deputy governor to reside in the Abyssinian capital. Whether this plan succeeds or not depends on whether the Port of Assab can be ceded to Abyssinia. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 4th)

(Paris) Yesterday afternoon, the Italian Ambassador Cerutti visited Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval, and the meeting lasted for half an hour. It is generally believed that although this meeting was at Cerutti's initiative, Laval took the opportunity to notify the Italian Ambassador of the suggestions made by the British and French experts as a result of their talks to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. News of the situation of these talks has been transmitted to Rome in recent days. It is said that the opinions of the British and French experts are now approaching each other, but an agreement has not yet been fully reached. The work of the experts is based on the method of exchanging land between Italy and Abyssinia, because this method is easier to draft, enough to make the League of Nations feel satisfied, and Italy and Abyssinia also have the possibility of directly reaching a compromise. In general, most of the suggestions made by the Committee of Five of the League of Nations Administrative Council in September have been abandoned by the British and French experts, who advocate that Abyssinia should maintain complete independence, and that before the Italo-Abyssinian dispute is completely resolved, it will not ask countries to provide financial and economic assistance under the supervision of the League of Nations. As for the proposed land exchange method, it is roughly that Italy demarcates a corridor in Eritrea that leads to the Red Sea, along with the Port of Assab, and grants it to Abyssinia, while Abyssinia cedes a piece of land between the northern Tigre province and French Somaliland to Italy. The holy city of Aksum is within the ceded area, but it still belongs to Abyssinia, and the city of Magale is also demarcated outside the area. As for southern Abyssinia, the land within 8 degrees north latitude and 38 or 40 degrees east longitude, including the Ogaden region, is all to be granted to Italy. In addition, the United Kingdom agrees to the eastern 40 degrees. According to the observation of some people here, although Mussolini did not approve of Eden's proposal in August, he may be willing to discuss the above methods. Informed sources believe that the above plan will enable Foreign Secretary Hoare and Laval to have greater possibilities in their talks on Saturday the 6th, and that no matter what attitude Italy and Abyssinia take, it will be enough to ease the international situation. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 5th)

British Warships Leave the Mediterranean, Commentators Say It is a Friendly Gesture to Italy

(London) Today, officials claimed that the British warships stationed in Gibraltar are now sailing out to cruise to a certain location in the Atlantic within the Strait. Commentators say this move is a friendly gesture to Italy. Well-informed circles in London point out that this statement is inaccurate, because the fleet always makes this cruise during exercises. Although the ships have left the Mediterranean, they will definitely not be far from the Strait of Gibraltar. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

Gibraltar The British Home Fleet stationed here left this morning and sailed to the open sea farther from the coast for exercises, scheduled to return here at the end of this week. In addition, the two largest British cruisers, the HMS Hawkins and the HMS Repulse, have also sailed to the Portuguese island of Madeira and other ports, scheduled to return to Gibraltar on the 18th of this month. According to informed sources, the HMS Hawkins is sailing to Madeira, and the HMS Repulse is sailing to Dakar, French Africa. Several other destroyers, including the HMS Keppel, sailed out of Huelva, Spain, for exercises. It is also said that this exercise has absolutely no political significance and is completely unrelated to the Abyssinian incident. The intention of the British Admiralty is that it is not appropriate for the Home Fleet stationed in Gibraltar to remain stationary for a long time, so it has made it sail to the open sea for exercises. Therefore, the exercise location should be within 20 miles of the Port of Gibraltar, so that it can be concentrated in the port within a few hours if necessary. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 5th)

Rome Also Denies Rumors

(Rome) Recently, there have been official rumors that the war situation on the front line is unfavorable. The government has taken strict measures to punish them. The fascist mouthpiece, the Italian People's Newspaper, also issued a warning about this matter, saying, "Anyone who officially spreads unfavorable news from the front line, no matter who they are, the police authorities will severely punish them without any leniency. This news is being spread by people from countries participating in the sanctions. All our citizens must not believe it." (Havas News Agency dispatch, 5th)

US Deputy Postmaster General Announces Pacific Aviation to Extend to China Soon, Implementable in One Month or Six Weeks, Negotiations Completed with Macao as Terminus

(Washington) Deputy Postmaster General Branch predicted today that the Pacific mail transport airline will be extended to China, and will be implementable in one month or six weeks. It was learned today that United Airlines has completed negotiations with the Portuguese side to use Macao as the terminus. However, the negotiations between the US government and the Chinese government on the transfer of mail after arriving in Macao have not yet been completed. According to the current plan, this mail will be handed over to the Chinese authorities in Macao. United Airlines is very satisfied with choosing Macao as the terminus. (国民电, 4th)

(San Francisco) United Airlines has signed a 20-year contract to lease the facilities of Mills Field Municipal Airport and expand it with an expenditure of $1,675,000. The naval authorities will build Alameda as a naval base, and the airline must give up the land within one year, so it must quickly find another aviation base so that San Francisco can become the permanent terminus of the Pacific airline. (国民电, 5th)

Midway Island The China Clipper flew to Honolulu from here at 10:12 this morning. (国民电, 4th)

Honolulu The China Clipper arrived here at 5:28 PM today, having completed the 1,300-mile journey from Midway Island to here. The plane will stay here overnight and will fly back to the Alameda base in California tomorrow morning. (国民电, 4th)

Three British Airships to Make a Far East Flight, Depart from Singapore in Mid-February, Via Manila, Hong Kong, Shanghai to Tokyo

(London) The Air Ministry announced today that the Royal Air Force's 205th Squadron, consisting of three airships carrying a total of 25 officers and crew members, is scheduled to depart from Singapore in mid-February for a return visit to Japan. The Japanese government has granted permission. This trip will pass through Manila, Hong Kong, Xiamen, and Shanghai to reach Japan. After arriving in Japan, it plans to continue to several places, returning via Hong Kong, then via Cam Ranh Bay, Indochina, and returning to Singapore in the second week of March. The entire journey is approximately 7,000 miles, led by Admiral Smith, Commander of the Royal Air Force in the Far East. The stay in Japan will be approximately one week. This is the first time the Royal Air Force has visited Japan. Because it needs to fly over and land at ports in other countries along the way, it is currently requesting the approval of the governments of the countries concerned. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

Atlantic Airline to Start Trial Flights Next Year and Open the Year After

(Washington) Today, Postmaster General Farley stated that he will request funds from the next Congress to open the Atlantic air mail service. Trial flights will begin next summer, and the official opening is expected in 1937. This route will be undertaken by an airline run by Americans, but because it is necessary to seek an airport abroad, it may also be undertaken jointly by American and foreign companies. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

(Washington) Aviation experts from Canada, Northern Ireland, Newfoundland, and the United Kingdom came here today to discuss the Atlantic air mail issue with US officials. They have been at the Ottawa Conference for several days. Postal Minister Flay said he is prepared to ask Congress to designate funds to open the airline at the appropriate time. (国民电, 4th)

Laval Prepares to Dissolve the Fascist League; Accepts All Demands of the Radical Party

(Paris) Last night, French Prime Minister Laval held important consultations with the leaders of the Radical Socialist Party, the result of which has increased the hope that the government will secure a victory in today's political debate in the Chamber of Deputies. According to reliable sources, Laval has accepted all the demands of the Radical Socialist Party, the most important of which is said to be the dissolution of the Fascist League. Those who support the government are now extremely optimistic about the outcome of today's debate in the Chamber of Deputies because Laval's actions have already secured the support of powerful elements within the Radical Socialist Party. Yesterday, the Radical Party continued its meeting to decide the party's attitude towards the government in the Chamber of Deputies today, but after further discussions, no compromise was reached, which is another favorable development for Laval. At the same time, the outflow of French gold in the past few days has greatly decreased. This is the result of the increase in bank interest rates and the strengthening of the national psyche. People are generally satisfied with this. Although the weekly report of the Bank of France declares that the outflow of gold in the week of November 28th was worth a total of 300 million francs, the report for next week will show a large decrease in the outflow of gold, as almost no one has withdrawn gold since December 1st, except for 3 million francs worth of gold that was withdrawn on November 30th. (Reuters, 5th)

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies continued its meeting this morning to discuss the activities of fascist groups. Members of the Central Right Party, such as Barton and Henri, spoke, questioning why the government was particularly tolerant of the extreme left-wing Popular Front. International Commercial Telegram

Reuters Special Commercial Report, December 5th

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today, 140 shillings and 11.5 pence, unchanged.

London Silver Market: Stable today, prices unchanged. Spot is 29 pence 0.1875, futures is 28 pence 0.8125. China and India sold slightly, the United States purchased.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market is stable. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was $4.933125, 0.0625 lower than the closing rate yesterday. After the first hour, it rose 0.0125, and then remained unchanged.

British-French: Unchanged at the opening, the price was 74 francs 90. After an hour, it rose 3 pounds sterling, and at noon it fell 2 pounds sterling. The price continued to fluctuate. At 1:00 PM, it rose 3 pounds sterling, and at 2:00 PM it fell back to 74 francs 91.

Cotton and Wheat

New York: The cotton market opened slightly lower, then the price rose slightly due to some buying. There are reports of increased exports. Everyone expects the next government estimate to decrease, but it is doubtful how much the US cotton storage organization will sell at the current price. There is also concern that cotton producers who have not yet signed contracts with the government may increase their cotton acreage.

Chicago Wheat: Today, the market fell 0.25 at the opening due to weakness in the Liverpool wheat market. The price continued to fall due to a large number of long positions being closed. Miscellaneous grains were unchanged at the opening, but quickly fell along with the price of wheat, and then recovered slightly.

Liverpool Cotton: Quiet this morning, prices fell slightly. At 1:00 PM, the January futures price was 6.46, down 1 pound sterling.

Liverpool Wheat: Very quiet this morning due to lack of exciting news. Flour manufacturers are still watching and waiting, and the industry is uneasy due to rumors that the Canadian authorities are planning to implement a more aggressive sales policy for wheat. At 1:00 PM, the December futures price was 5 shillings 11 pence 0.375, down 0.625.

Rubber

London: The market situation is stable today. The transaction price for April-June futures is 6 pence 0.4375, 0.0625 higher than yesterday's closing price.

New York: The market opened today up 3 pounds sterling because of the improved situation in the London market. Continued good demand caused prices to rise further, but later there were long positions closing, and at the time of the telegram, the price had fallen back to the opening price.

Securities

New York: Continued progress this morning. Prices were mostly slightly higher, except for railroad stocks. Public utility stocks saw the most significant gains. Although there was general profit-taking later, the market situation remained stable. The Dow Jones average of 30 industrial stocks opened at 144.27, up 23 pounds sterling. Italy and Abyssinia at War for Two Months; No Major Battle Yet; Abyssinian Troops Still Heavily Mobilizing in the North

(London) Abyssinian vehicles are now advancing from the Aushango Lake area towards Magal, 65 miles southeast of Adowa. The war between Italy and Abyssinia has lasted for two months, and no major battle has yet occurred. A major battle may begin within days. Abyssinian troops are commanded by General Gazar, including the Abyssinian King's Guards. The offensive is equipped with rifles, machine guns, and new artillery. Their vanguard has been sighted by Italian outposts stationed about 15 miles south of Magal. Italian troops are delighted that a real battle is about to begin. At the same time, small groups of Abyssinian soldiers are still harassing Italian troops in the Danakil area. Italian troops claim to have occupied half of the Danakil area. While attacking Magal, Abyssinian troops may also take the offensive on the southern front, hoping to coordinate their efforts. The "Hindenburg Line" built by the Abyssinian troops on the southern front has recently been completed. Junior officers strongly advocate an attack, but senior officers have not yet agreed. (Reuters, 5th)

Asmara: The troops under Abyssinian General Kekesam are still heavily mobilizing today, indicating that the first major battle in the Italian-Abyssinian war will take place on the northern front within days. Reports received here today state that General Seyoum, who was twice rumored to be dead, is now leading 30,000 troops towards Amba Alagi to join forces with General Kazar. (National, 4th) Asmara learned today that a large Abyssinian force, carrying the latest military equipment, attempted to cut off the Italian defense line from Magal to Duro after contacting Italian outposts in Magal. It was announced here today that four regular Italian troops were killed in the battle of Dèbri. (National, 4th)

Djibouti: It is reported that Abyssinian troops attacked the Italian defense line in Seri Kot, south of Magal, on Tuesday. The two sides fought fiercely for a long time. Italian troops claimed to have repelled the offensive. (Reuters, 5th)

Former Commander of Italian East African Forces Returns Home; Arrives Quietly Without Welcome

(Rome) Former Commander-in-Chief of the Italian East African Forces, General De Bono, quietly arrived in Italy yesterday, unnoticed even by newspaper reporters. When the General arrived in Syracuse, local officials greeted him. He is expected to arrive in Rome today. There are no reports of any welcome plans from the government or the public. The General is of short stature, with white hair and sharp eyes. He established military achievements in the Libyan War and World War I. Mussolini greatly valued him when he was a soldier. After Mussolini came to power, he appointed him as his military advisor. He successively served as the head of the police department, commander of the militia, and governor of Tripolitania. In 1929, when the government was reorganized, he was appointed Minister of Colonial Affairs. His position as Commander-in-Chief of Italian East Africa was replaced by General Badoglio in mid-November, and he has now returned to his country depressed. (Reuters, 5th)

(Rome) Italian East African Commander-in-Chief General Badoglio said at the time of his inauguration that he would not engage in propaganda, and he has now fulfilled his promise, reporting only to the Italian High Command that "both fronts remain in their original state." (National, 4th)

(Rome) The King and Queen of Italy have moved countless Italians after donating their 39th wedding anniversary gold rings to the government to increase Italy's cash reserves. It is expected that on December 18, Italy's "Day of Faith," a large pile of gold rings will be placed in front of the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, which will then be melted down and cast into gold bars. The government announced today that those who donate gold rings will be given stainless steel rings by the government. The government also announced today that the King and Queen of Italy have canceled their New Year's reception for foreign guests, demonstrating the royal family's efforts to cooperate with austerity measures. (National, 4th)

Motion for Independence Defeated in the South Irish Parliament; No Basis for Negotiations with Britain

(London) A motion was introduced in the South Irish Free State Parliament requesting that the Free State government ask the League of Nations to recognize Ireland's independence. If the League of Nations does not grant the request, then the Free State should withdraw from the League of Nations. This motion was put to a vote today and defeated by a majority. Another motion criticizing the policies of the Free State government has been passed, with only one vote against it. Prime Minister de Valera claimed that even if South Ireland's membership in the League of Nations does not benefit South Ireland, it cannot prevent it from pursuing national unification and independence. As for the rumors that Britain and the Free State are negotiating, there is no basis for them. National freedom is not a dream and can eventually be achieved. (Reuters, 5th)

Five Nations' Representatives Gather in London; Naval Conference Becomes Increasingly Imminent; Opening Ceremony Next Monday; Many Conflicting Opinions Between the United States and Japan

(London) Representatives from Britain, France, and Italy attending the Naval Conference will arrive in London on Friday in order to participate in the opening ceremony on Monday. The Japanese delegation has now arrived in Britain. The government originally planned to host a banquet on Monday evening to entertain the representatives attending the Naval Conference, but due to the death of Princess Victoria, the banquet has now been postponed. (Reuters, 4th)

(London) The chief Japanese delegates to the London Naval Conference, Nagano and Nagai, visited the Admiralty this morning to pay their respects to the First Lord of the Admiralty, Monsell. The French delegation, led by Vice Admiral Robert, the Italian delegation, led by Rear Admiral Piscya, and the US delegation, led by Norman Davis, are all scheduled to arrive here tomorrow. The Italian, French, and American representatives are all scheduled to meet with the First Lord of the Admiralty, Monsell, on Sunday afternoon. (Havas, 5th)

(London) Experts said today that the current international balance of power has been disturbed by the African war. Recently, world attention has refocused on the upcoming Five-Power Naval Conference. For several weeks, the generally accepted comparative strength of the world's naval powers has changed, as the air power of each country should be given more attention when calculating naval strength in the future. The tense situation between Britain and Italy caused by the Italian-Abyssinian conflict has shown that the power of the air force can prevent the British Mediterranean Fleet, at least a part of it, from using Malta as a base of operations like the iron wall of the past, and it must retreat to Alexandria and Gibraltar. This matter deserves attention. This is enough to show that naval commanders are deeply concerned about the power of bombers. Furthermore, the African war has made it impossible for Britain's naval power to take care of matters outside of Europe, and Japan's comparative strength has naturally increased, as Japan can now act without hesitation along the coast of East Asia. This naval conference was convened by the British government in accordance with the provisions of the Washington Treaty of February 6, 1922. The treaty stipulates that a conference must be convened to re-discuss if one country gives notice of abandonment. The Japanese government notified all signatory countries on February 6, 1934, declaring its intention to terminate the treaty on December 31, 1936, in accordance with Article 23 of the treaty. Therefore, Britain re-invited the United States, Japan, France, and Italy to meet in London. Naval experts here all say that if this conference cannot resolve the issue of the size of each country's fleet in the future, then the international arms race and the danger of war may follow one another. Now that the conference is near, observers have many doubts about the future of the conference. Britain and Japan have both expressed dissatisfaction with the existing restrictions, namely the Washington and London treaties, while Washington still insists on the 5:5:3 ratio. Although the London Treaty did not reduce the total tonnage of each country's battleships, it did limit the number of ships. Therefore, no giant ships have been built in recent years. If a new treaty cannot be established after this conference, then the cost of one ship, which requires US$20 million, will increase again. (National, 4th)

(London) The Japanese representatives attending the London Naval Conference stated today that political issues cannot be separated from naval issues. Their position is based on a statement from the Tokyo Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which states that a naval agreement cannot be concluded until there is a complete understanding of the political issues of the world situation. The Japanese representative stated today in his private capacity that at this conference, they are not prepared to discuss the size of warships until all political issues have been resolved. The reason why they have adopted this position is that the naval ratio issue in the Washington Treaty is inextricably linked to the security and reputation of Japan and other countries. After Japan expressed this view, diplomatic experts believed that the hope for this conference has been completely eliminated. (National, 4th)

(Washington) The State Department expressed surprise upon hearing Japan's claim that discussing political issues at the naval conference is unavoidable. Well-informed observers believe that the United States welcomes following the scope of the 1922 Washington Conference and continuing the current naval ratio in order to seek a comprehensive solution to the Far East issue, but since Japan does not want to accept the ratio system, the United States will not agree to discuss political issues at the naval conference. (National, 4th)

(Tokyo) It is rumored that the Japanese plenipotentiary Nagano declared in London a disarmament policy, saying that he was not opposed to abolishing submarines and welcomed the conclusion of a Pacific non-aggression treaty, but this is completely contrary to Japan's policy and is likely to be a misrepresentation. Therefore, today the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued the following statement of confirmation: The Japanese plenipotentiary delegation must seek instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Navy before issuing a statement, but there has been no request for instructions so far, so it is not believed that this statement was issued. The abolition of submarines runs counter to the Japanese government's disarmament policy, so it is not believed that it was stated. Submarines are defensive weapons, so in inferior naval countries, they can achieve military goals economically. Therefore, if the countries do not agree to completely abolish offensive weapons, Japan will never agree to abolish submarines. A Pacific non-aggression agreement, which seeks to ensure the security of the Pacific through group organization, is contrary to the Japanese diplomatic policy of East Asianism. Therefore, Japan will not discuss naval issues unless it agrees to a Far East non-threat non-aggression agreement. The existence of Article 19 of the Washington Treaty, which restricts the fortification of the Pacific, is a matter that Japan is prepared to respond to if proposed by the countries concerned, but it will not actively propose it. (Dentsu, 5th)

(London) Admiral Nagano, the chief Japanese representative to the London Naval Conference, recently made a statement to a reporter from Havas, saying, "The main basis of Japanese policy is security. We believe that security must be equal, so we believe that the right to equal naval power should be a prerequisite for the establishment of all agreements. In our view, the right to equal naval power is equal to guaranteeing our country's security. In short, only the Japanese Navy Department has the right to determine the scope of our country's needs to cope with the environment." The reporter then asked what Japan's opinion would be on the issue of limiting total tonnage if the Naval Conference recognized Japan's right to equal power. Admiral Nagano replied, "We are now beginning to discuss this. We will discuss the maximum limit on total tonnage with the delegations of the various countries in a spirit of compromise." Referring to the qualitative restrictions on the navy, Nagano said, "Japan's attitude will depend on how Japan's first demand (namely, the right to equal naval power) and the issue of total tonnage are resolved." When asked whether the Naval Conference would discuss the issue of the fortification of Pacific islands, Nagano said that Japan would not object to discussing this issue if other delegations raised it. (Havas, 4th)

Tolstoy's Death Anniversary

(Moscow, TASS, November 14) Tolstoy was a world-renowned writer. He passed away in the small room of the stationmaster at Astapovo station on November 20th, twenty-five years ago, leaving behind only his villa. In his diary, this great writer once recorded such an incident: in a dream, he buried his own fear and shame in front of the oppressed people in the desert because he was powerless to liberate enslaved Russia. Tolstoy's philosophical and religious views, of course, cannot be accepted by the working masses, but his works, especially his novels, have had a wide circulation since the October Revolution. Lenin repeatedly praised the importance of Tolstoy's works, exposing the oppression of the Tsarist government and revealing the deep contradictions between the rich and the poor. At the same time, Lenin also vigorously attacked his doctrine of non-resistance and his social thought. After the establishment of the Soviet government, even during the civil war, the circulation of Tolstoy's works increased. 700,000 copies of his books were published this year. In the past seventeen years, 11,650,000 copies of Tolstoy's works have been published in thirty-two different languages in the Soviet Union. The Soviet government has decided to ask Tolstoy's close friend, Chertkov, to compile Tolstoy's complete works in ninety-five volumes. These include thirteen volumes of Tolstoy's diaries that have never been published before. During the 25th anniversary of Tolstoy's death, factories and cultural institutions in the Soviet Union gave lectures and reports on Tolstoy's life and works. Exhibitions of Tolstoy's works were held in Moscow, Leningrad, and other cities. Tolstoy's former residence has been turned into a museum by the Soviet government. All the furnishings are exactly the same as when Tolstoy was alive. Tens of thousands of workers in the Soviet Union visit this residence every year. Now the Soviet government is also going to issue commemorative stamps for Tolstoy. A grand memorial service for Tolstoy will be held in Moscow on November 20th. On the 21st, Soviet writers and artists will visit Tolstoy's residence again.

New Air Route from Crimea to the Caucasus

(Yalta, TASS, November 14) The new air route between Odessa and Batumi is now nearing completion. After this, transportation between the ports along the Black Sea coast will be more convenient. When airplanes fly on this route, they will land in Sevastopol, Yalta, Feodosia, and Kerch in Crimea. Five amphibious aircraft will fly on this route. This air route is extremely important for the economic and cultural development of the Black Sea coast, as it will be used for air mail and passengers, and it will be used as a transportation tool for most travelers.

Legislative Yuan Celebrates its Seventh Anniversary

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held a ceremony at 11:00 AM on the 5th to celebrate its seventh anniversary. Central representative Wu Jingheng, National Government representative Deng Jiayan, and guests Qin Zhen, Jiao Yitang, Chen Zhaoying, Ma Chaojun, and Wang Yongbin attended. All members of the Legislative Yuan and staff, led by President Sun, participated. Beforehand, the Yuan decorated the entrance and auditorium with pine branches and colorful flowers. After President Sun presided over the ceremony and led the attendees in paying their respects, he delivered a report, first describing the general situation of the Legislative Yuan in the past year, and finally encouraging his colleagues to intensify the work of the Legislative Yuan, enrich the spirit of legislation, and continue to serve the country, so as to find a way out for the country and the nation in difficult and dangerous situations. Wu Jingheng and Deng Jiayan gave speeches, praising the satisfactory achievements of the Legislative Yuan in the past and informing them that the central government had resolved to accept the entire draft constitution formulated by the Legislative Yuan and scheduled it to be announced on May 5th of next year. Their hard work in drafting the constitution seemed to have received great consolation. After the speeches, all members of the Legislative Yuan applauded enthusiastically. Qin Zhen said that legislation is the work of nation-building, assisting all members of the Legislative Yuan to continue to shoulder the important task of nation-building. He also elaborated on his views on reforming China's judiciary after returning from his trip to Europe, explaining the misunderstandings caused in the legislative community in the past, and hoped that all members of the Legislative Yuan would go deep into the people and publicize the legislative spirit of the draft constitution before it is promulgated, in order to win the people's approval. Wang Yongbin said in his speech that he expressed his appreciation to his old colleagues in the Legislative Yuan, apart from praising his personal service in the Examination and Judicial Yuan after leaving the Legislative Yuan, he has strictly enforced the law and is worthy of the trust. He also regarded not participating in drafting the constitution as a matter of regret. Finally, he hoped that legislation should change with the times and facts, and especially hoped that the laws on compulsory execution, prison detention centers, and bar associations would be passed as soon as possible. The ceremony ended at 12:00 noon. They then went to the West Garden of the Yuan for a group photo. President Sun invited all participants to a meal at the Yuan. During the meal, they raised their glasses and made toasts, with both solemnity and humor, and everyone had a good time before dispersing. After the meal, various entertainment activities were performed, and the atmosphere was warm. The Yuan announced that the 5th would be a holiday to celebrate, and the regular meeting on the 6th would also be suspended. (Central News Agency, 5th)

Hong Kong Authorities Devise Methods to Stabilize Foreign Exchange, Nationalize Private Silver, Establish Foreign Exchange Reserve Committee

(Hong Kong) The Hong Kong Legislative Council resolved on the 5th to purchase silver from the people and establish a Foreign Exchange Reserve Committee to stabilize foreign exchange rates. Individuals are prohibited from holding more than ten dollars in silver; violators will be detained and fined. Future transactions will be limited to legal tender and banknotes from the three banks of HSBC, Standard Chartered, and Mercantile Bank. A Foreign Exchange Advisory Committee will be established to determine exchange rates. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Hong Kong government issued an order today to nationalize privately held silver and establish an exchange control fund. Although this measure does not explicitly stipulate the stabilization of the Hong Kong dollar's value, its effect will grant the Financial Secretary full authority to manage exchange rates. It is noted that on November 9th, the Hong Kong government prohibited the export of all kinds of silver. Today's move is merely the second step in that direction. The government order briefly states that all note-issuing banks should hand over all silver coins and large silver bars held as banknote reserves to the Hong Kong Treasury. The Treasury will issue securities in exchange. Under the Treasury's management, an exchange fund will be established to adjust the exchange rate of the Hong Kong dollar. The Financial Secretary will consult with the Exchange Fund Advisory Committee on management matters. The Financial Secretary will chair the committee, and other members will be appointed by the Governor of Hong Kong. All silver coins and silver bars turned over to the Treasury will be paid into the Exchange Fund, and payments for the surrendered silver will also be made from the Exchange Fund. Anyone holding British silver dollars, Mexican silver dollars, Hong Kong subsidiary coinage, or silver bars with a value exceeding ten dollars must hand them over to the Treasury within one month. Those who pay in silver coins will receive Hong Kong banknotes at face value, while those who pay in silver bars will receive Hong Kong banknotes at a price of one dollar and twenty-eight cents per ounce. Violators will be subject to imprisonment for up to one year, confiscation of silver coins and silver bars, and a fine of up to twice the value of the confiscated items. All or part of this Exchange Fund may be held in Hong Kong banknotes or other currencies, or the Financial Secretary may use it to purchase securities approved by the British Secretary of State for the Colonies. The Financial Secretary may buy and sell such currencies or securities, but all such transactions must be for immediate delivery. The Financial Secretary may borrow money for the Exchange Fund, but the amount of debt may not exceed HK$30 million. Those holding Treasury licenses may deposit silver. The Financial Secretary may permit anyone to store silver in an amount deemed necessary for their business. The Attorney General of Hong Kong, Alabaster, issued a statement regarding this order, explaining its purpose and reasons. He stated that the purpose of this order is to establish the government's control over Hong Kong's foreign exchange to prevent improper fluctuations. Legally issued bank notes should be legal tender locally. Note-issuing banks must turn over all silver coins and silver bars previously held as note reserves to the Treasury, which will issue them with bonds as collateral for the notes. These bonds, issued under the Currency Ordinance of 1935, are a type of non-interest-bearing debt instrument of the Hong Kong government, which the Hong Kong Financial Secretary may redeem at his discretion. When presenting the Exchange Fund proposal, the Attorney General stated that if the Hong Kong market were only for the use of the Hong Kong people, the currency in its current abnormal state might be allowed to exist until the world situation clears up. However, this market is not like that, and the Hong Kong dollar is in danger of being subject to violent fluctuations due to the activities of speculators from other ports, which may harm the interests of legitimate trade in Hong Kong. The Hong Kong authorities recently discussed coping methods in detail with the leaders of the three note-issuing banks, HSBC, Mercantile Bank, and Chartered Bank. The leaders of the three banks fully agreed to establish an Exchange Fund under the chairmanship of the Financial Secretary, supplemented by an advisory committee. The Exchange Fund established in this way will receive all cash silver, and after the cash silver is nationalized, no one holding cash silver can export it. In the future, when the system is fully established and the silver export ban can be cancelled, there may be profits and losses arising from the sale of silver. The Hong Kong government has decided on the only correct method: to use the silver reserves to pay for banknotes. All profits and losses on the handling of this silver reserve will belong to the Exchange Fund. The prices at which the Exchange Fund buys and sells foreign exchange will not be made public. All fund accounts will be audited according to the methods approved by the Secretary of State. All profits and losses arising from the operation of this fund will be listed in the government accounts. (5th Reuter's dispatch)

Historical Facts of Competition Among Britain, France, and Italy in Abyssinia (Continued)

— Special

As the saying goes, "He who laughs last laughs best"; the winner of a race can also be disqualified. Abyssinian soldiers garrisoned in the sandy lowlands ran out of provisions, and then a major flood occurred, so they dropped their national flag and hurried away. Marchand still held out, but he had no large army to help him. Kitchener, after severely defeating the Muslims who were blocking his way, led his victorious soldiers in a mighty march to Fashoda. The French government then ordered the stubborn Marchand to retreat as soon as he saw an opportunity. As a result, the English flag flew firmly over Fashoda, and to this day, it still waves in the wind, and from the Cape of Good Hope to Cairo, all are within the reach of British power. France has been relegated to a secondary position in East Africa.

In the meantime, France used rifles to assist Emperor Menelik of Abyssinia in destroying a branch of the Italian army that had invaded Abyssinia from the north. In 1897, France also concluded a friendship agreement with Abyssinia, stipulating that Djibouti would be the official port of the Abyssinian Empire. Once the new railway is built, the commerce of an area larger than any country in Europe except Russia will be entirely transported to a French port. Menelik's move was tantamount to giving the key to his country to Paris. Furthermore, French merchants could enjoy preferential treatment in Abyssinia, and France also obtained other privileges. The construction of the new road began. These were all things that happened before Kitchener arrived at Fashoda. After Kitchener arrived at Fashoda, British prestige increased in East Africa, and the British representative in the Abyssinian capital became very active.

In 1902, Britain and Menelik concluded a preferential treaty regarding the use of water from the Blue Nile River and even obtained the right to build a railway from the British colony of Zeila through Abyssinia to Sudan. This was a terrible obstacle in the middle of the French railway, making Djibouti seem no longer to be the main gateway to Abyssinia. At the same time, the French company failed, and the railway project was stopped. Later, France reached an understanding with the other two most relevant major powers, allowing France to build roads to the Abyssinian capital, but not to approach the Nile River, allowing Britain to use the waters of Lake Tana and the Blue Nile, and allowing Italy to enjoy most of the economic concessions in Abyssinia and to build a crescent-shaped railway from Eritria in the north through western Abyssinia to Italian Somaliland in the south. In the future, if the Abyssinian Empire split up, each country could do whatever it wanted within its designated sphere of influence. At first, Emperor Menelik of Abyssinia knew nothing about this treaty and never recognized it. Although this treaty became the basis of relations between Abyssinia and the great powers, it was still a secret document.

In 1908, although Menelik was extremely unwilling, he finally concluded a treaty with France regarding the railway project. Nine years later, after extreme hardship, the Djibouti to Abyssinian capital railway was fortunately completed. This enterprise now belongs to the French Republic and is very profitable. This is the only real result of a hundred years of international intrigue. This road now transports 80% of the trade goods between Abyssinia and foreign countries and transports 95% of the travelers entering and leaving Abyssinia. The shares total 34,000 shares, and 2,500 shares were transferred to Italy earlier this year.

In 1915, France and Britain concluded a secret treaty in London, guaranteeing Italy that if it joined the Allied Powers in World War I, it would enjoy rich benefits in Abyssinia. France never fulfilled its promise, but earlier this year, it granted Italy some trivial land concessions, seeming to allow Italy freedom of action in Abyssinia.

In 1923, when the League of Nations discussed Abyssinia's accession, France spoke highly of Abyssinia. In short, no major power has helped Abyssinia as much as France. (Translated from an article by R.H. Markham in the Christian Science Monitor)

Vietnam Levies Heavy Import Duties on Chinese Silk

(Nanjing) The import duty rate on Chinese silk in Vietnam was increased before the Sino-French Vietnamese commercial treaty was concluded. After the recent announcement of the commercial treaty, in addition to the regular tax and basic tax, a balancing tax is also levied, requiring 25% of the value. The import of Chinese silk into Vietnam is subject to heavy taxes, totaling more than 100% of the value. The Shanghai Municipal Motor Silk Weaving Factory and the Silk Industry Association fear that the sales of Chinese silk will be stopped due to this. At the same time, Chinese businessmen in Vietnam have telegraphed to complain. Therefore, the Shanghai Silk Industry Association has petitioned the government to negotiate with France to demand efforts to improve the situation in order to promote the export of Chinese silk. This case is currently being reviewed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for negotiation with France. (5th Special Dispatch)

Judicial Yuan Interprets Ambiguity Regarding Bigamy

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan, based on a request from the Guangxi Higher Court for an interpretation of the ambiguity regarding bigamy, has made the following decision at the unified interpretation of laws and regulations meeting of the Yuan: If a husband goes out and his whereabouts are unknown for more than three years, it is indeed a reason for divorce according to law, but if a divorce or declaration of death has not been finalized, the marital relationship still exists. If the wife remarries, it cannot be said that it is not bigamy. The order has been telegraphed for notification. (5th Special Dispatch)

Taiwan Commodity Shipments to Xiamen Decrease

From Over 400 Pieces to 200 Pieces; Water Passengers Carrying Goods Also Decreasing

Xiamen Correspondence: Xiamen and Taiwan are only separated by a strait. Ships can arrive in just twelve hours. Consequently, the number of Taiwanese products and Japanese goods passing through Taiwan to Xiamen has been extremely large. Besides agricultural products and bulky items stored in warehouses, textiles and sundries were mostly carried by so-called "water passengers." As a result, each ship arriving from Taiwan often had five or six hundred passengers who came specifically to carry goods. The goods were all packed in luggage. Customs inspections often clashed with these water passengers, resulting in significant tax evasion. This summer, the Xiamen Customs Commissioner and the Japanese Consul agreed on an accord regarding Taiwanese water passengers carrying goods, limiting each ship to four hundred people, each allowed to carry four cubic meters of goods. Before the implementation of legal tender (fa bi), foreign exchange rates were extremely high, with 130-140 Japanese yen being worth 100 Chinese yuan. Due to the low exchange rate of the Japanese yen, dumping was effective, and Japanese goods flooded in. After the agreement was implemented and taxes were levied per item, each ship still had two to three hundred water passengers, carrying around 400 pieces of goods. Since the implementation of legal tender, foreign exchange rates have been suppressed, with 100 Chinese yuan being worth only 103 Japanese yen, and the rate is stable. The profits from Taiwanese goods coming to Xiamen are no longer as substantial as before. Furthermore, customs inspections for silver are extremely strict. Each ship departing often has three to five thousand yuan worth of silver discovered. Therefore, the number of Taiwanese water passengers coming to Xiamen with goods has been decreasing daily recently. In the past two weeks, each ship has had no more than a hundred water passengers, sometimes only dozens, and the number of goods has decreased from over four hundred pieces to just over two hundred or a hundred pieces. In addition, in the past month, customs have uncovered silver ingots and silver dollars worth over 50,000 yuan in total. Other items, such as smuggled white sugar, kerosene, textiles, matches, ginseng, seafood, beef tendons, medicinal materials, and ships, are estimated at around 100,000 yuan. On the 3rd, the ship departing from Guangdong bound for Taiwan only uncovered over 500 yuan worth of silver, which is also much less than before. (December 4th)

Fujianese People Oppose the Imposition of Rice Tax

Zhangzhou-Shima Rice Tax Has Already Been Implemented; Xiamen Chamber of Commerce Discussing Relief Measures

Xiamen Correspondence, December 1st: The date for the Fujian Provincial Government to implement the rice tax in Zhangzhou Prefecture. Rice merchants in Zhangzhou and Shima have risen up in opposition. Prior to this, they resolved to suspend purchasing rice from rural areas and exporting rice for ten days, starting from November 26th, and scheduled another meeting for December 5th to discuss further actions. It is understood that only Zhangzhou Prefecture in Fujian Province produces rice. Since the imposition of import duties on foreign rice, Xiamen and Quanzhou have relied exclusively on Zhangzhou rice, abandoning foreign rice. In Xiamen City alone, the daily demand is a thousand bags. Since the rice merchants in Zhangzhou and Shima have suspended transportation, rice prices in Xiamen have risen immediately. As of the 3rd, each dan (a unit of weight) has increased by half a yuan compared to the previous week, and by around two yuan compared to the previous month. Over a hundred Shima rice ships have suspended operations due to the transportation stoppage, and thousands of people have lost their jobs. Including family members, no less than several thousand people are facing threats to their livelihoods. Overseas Chinese businessmen Lin Bingxiang, Hu Wenhu, Chen Yanqian, and Xiamen University President Lin Wenqing jointly telegraphed the central and provincial governments, requesting the withdrawal of the order. On November 30th, the provincial government replied by telegram, stating approximately: "The Zhangzhou Prefecture national expenditure surcharges have been excessively numerous and the tax amounts have been heavy. Now, to alleviate the burden on the people, an order has been issued to abolish them all from December 1st. The funds for the local defense forces will be managed centrally by the provincial government. At this time of depleted financial resources, it has been resolved to implement a rice tax in Zhangzhou Prefecture to slightly offset the deficit. We hope for your understanding and support as much as possible." On December 1st, rice tax collection bureaus were established and implemented in Zhangzhou and Shima. On the same day, the provincial government issued an order to abolish thirty-seven types of security surcharges and miscellaneous taxes in Zhangzhou Prefecture, including: (1) Longxi security fee, West Creek business tax surcharge, Shima business tax surcharge, North Creek business tax surcharge, Hongdong business tax surcharge, sugar industry business tax surcharge, Northwest Creek paper industry business tax surcharge, Shima livestock tax surcharge, Zhangzhou guard donation surcharge of 10%, Jinzhou vehicle donation surcharge of 10%, surcharges for various township apportionment red material donations, banquet surcharge of 10%, firecracker donation surcharge of 10%, newspaper surcharge, ash donation surcharge, Shima gold leaf donation surcharge of 10%, Zhangzhou flower donation surcharge of 10%, Shima flower guard donation surcharge of 10%; (2) Security troop fees, West Creek business tax surcharge of 20%, North Creek business tax surcharge of 20%, West Creek paper industry tax surcharge of 20%, Zhangzhou tobacco and alcohol tax surcharge of 20%, fruit business surcharge of 20%, Shima livestock surcharge of 20%, Jiangdong business tax surcharge of 20%, Shima business surcharge of 20%, red material donation surcharge of 20%, banquet donation surcharge of 20%, firecracker donation surcharge of 20%, ash donation surcharge of 20%, Shima gold leaf donation surcharge of 20%, daffodil surcharge of 20%, Zhangzhou flower donation surcharge of 20%, Shima flower donation surcharge of 20%, Zhangzhou seafood surcharge of 20%, Zhangzhou sugar industry tax surcharge of 20%, Zhangzhou guard donation surcharge of 20%, Zhangzhou vehicle donation of 20%, as well as vegetable and cattle donations, etc.

The first to be affected by the rice merchants' transportation stoppage is Xiamen. As of the 3rd, the city's rice reserves are only sufficient to last for one week. The Rice Industry Association met with the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce on the 3rd, requesting that the city's various trade associations be convened quickly to discuss relief measures, and that a telegram be sent again in the name of the general assembly to the National Government's Ministry of Finance and the Rural Reconstruction Committee, as well as the provincial government, to immediately abolish the rice tax to benefit the people's food supply and avoid a rice panic. After receiving the letter, the Chamber of Commerce decided to convene a general assembly on the 5th to discuss the matter. At the same time, the Shima civilian ship and steamship associations also telegraphed the National Government's Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, and the Fujian-Zhejiang Surveillance Commissioner, stating approximately that the rice ship stoppage had resulted in thousands of people losing their jobs and requesting the withdrawal of the rice tax order. According to the Financial Department's plan this summer to reorganize Fujian Province's finances, the total amount of security troop fees, surcharges, and miscellaneous taxes for all counties in the province is over two million yuan annually. In reality, the burden on the people is even greater. It was decided that, in addition to retaining the land tax and slaughter tax surcharges to be directly remitted to the provincial treasury, all other items would be abolished, and the troop fees would be directly allocated by the provincial government. The plan was approved by the provincial government and scheduled to be implemented on December 1st. However, there are ten security troops and civilian militias in each county, and the expenses are very large. Therefore, it was agreed to collect a rice tax in Zhangzhou Prefecture as one of the ways to offset the deficit. The Zhangzhou Prefecture rice tax originated during Chen Jiongming's驻漳州 (stationed in Zhangzhou) era in the 7th year of the Republic (1918), and continued until the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). In order to protect rural areas, the central government levied import duties on foreign rice and promoted the circulation of rice throughout the country, and ordered the abolition of rice taxes throughout the country. The Jinzhou Prefecture rice tax was abolished at this time. This current implementation is in reality a re-imposition. (December 4th)

Suzhou Accidental Discharge of Firearm Leads to Death of Opium Den Employee

Yu Zhi, the Tiebao Chief (local security officer) of Lingtie Township, Suzhou, and training instructor for the merchant corps, was at a local opium den on the 4th. His personal sidearm accidentally discharged. With a bang, Ji Lejin, an employee of the opium den, immediately fell to the ground, dead. Following on-site verification from personnel sent by the District Procuratorate, they determined that it was an accidental discharge. On the 5th, the person who caused the accident, Yu Kuozhi, and the owner of the opium den, Dai Qu, were transferred to the Public Security Bureau for detention and will be sent to the District Procuratorate on the 6th for further investigation and handling.

Wuxi Robberies Rampant Amidst Winter Defense Efforts

Sheng Yinsheng, a resident of Cai Gengshang, the seventh Jia of the fifth Bao of Meicun Township in the Second District (from Jiangyin, over fifty years old, with a limp), who has been guarding the ancestral hall for Cai Jinyuan, was suddenly approached by more than ten bandits around one o'clock in the evening the other day. The bandits were wearing headscarves and blue cloth clothes, looking like fishermen from Jiangbei. Each was carrying a wooden club or short knife. After breaking down the door, they immediately restrained Yinsheng, stripped him of his clothes, tied him up with rope, and threatened him into silence. They wantonly searched and looted the premises. In the end, they stole over ten dan of rice, as well as clothes and other items, resulting in a loss of over two hundred yuan. However, because Yinsheng was tied up naked, he could not withstand the cold and no one came to his rescue. By dawn, he was on the verge of death. As of now, the case has not been reported to the county for arrest and investigation. In addition, the home of Cao Xingren, located in a thatched shack near the Shiqiao mound in the Tenth District, was also robbed by five bandits who entered the premises to carry out their robbery. Afterwards, police officers Sun Chuan'ying and others from the Wuqiao Police Station of the Fifth Sub-bureau and the Dawangmiao guard post apprehended the bandits Qian Zirong, Cao Rongzhang, Hu Shengbao, Chen Amao, and Zhao Renbao, and transferred them to the main bureau. On the 5th, they were transferred to the court for interrogation and detention. Furthermore, the vehicle patrol team of the Sixth Security Brigade apprehended two thugs, Li Chao and Yu Xiuzhen, near Dongting on the 5th and handed them over to the county government. The newly appointed county magistrate, Long Tiyao, personally held a court hearing, and as a result, ordered them to be detained together, pending investigation and handling.
