Education Broadcasting Special

Our Country's Scientific Research Undertakings (Continued)

— Ding Wenjiang, Director-General of the Academia Sinica

(Speech to Students of Chinese Secondary Schools on November 26th)

The First Geological Survey is an extremely poor organization. When it began to organize in the fifth year of the Republic (1916), it was expected to receive 120,000 yuan per year. From the fifth year of the Republic to the fifteenth year of the Republic, the actual funding received each year averaged only 50,000 yuan. At the lowest point, it was less than 30,000 yuan. Even now, the funding provided by the government is only 72,000 yuan. The difficulties faced by those involved can be imagined. However, it is precisely because of its poverty that it has avoided much political interference. Because funding is low, salaries are relatively low, and fieldwork is an extremely arduous task. From very early on, everyone knew that the Geological Survey was extremely demanding but the treatment was very poor. At first, some people would randomly recommend people to the director, but later, unless someone was truly interested in geology, they would shake their heads and be unwilling to join when the Geological Survey was mentioned. Therefore, in a very turbulent political environment, the Geological Survey was able to avoid being infected by it. Since the Republic, the heads of any government organization have often changed. However, the Geological Survey has only ever had two directors. The current director, Mr. Weng Wenhao, has been in office for fourteen years. The ministers and acting ministers of the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and the Ministry of Industry, who have jurisdiction over him, have changed more than twenty times! Because it is poor, it cannot support idlers, so the director can remain in his position for a long time. This is the first condition for the success of the Geological Survey.

Second, since its establishment, the Geological Survey has focused on practical problems. Not only have they discovered many new mines, but those who survey geology and mineral resources are constantly helping those who develop mines. Whether it is surveying mine area maps or geological maps, analyzing mineral properties, or determining drilling locations, as long as they are genuine mine developers, the Geological Survey is willing to help them work and plan. Neither individuals nor organizations receive any compensation. Therefore, people in the mining industry all know that the Geological Survey is their friend. When political difficulties arise, everyone comes out to speak for it. Moreover, in these twenty years, private donations to it have amounted to nearly 200,000 yuan. The library, dissection room, paleontology and fuel research laboratory, and seismology room of the Geological Survey in Beiping were all built with private donations. It is likely that the Geological Survey is the only government research organization to receive such large amounts of private donations.

Third, the Geological Survey is able to fully utilize foreign scholars. In recent years, many young people studying science have been influenced by nationalism and are often unwilling to cooperate with or be guided by foreigners. They do not know that this is a big mistake. Science was originally a product of Western Europe. Europeans and Americans have been studying science for at least 150 years. We have only been doing it for twenty years. Of course, they are better than us, and we must cooperate with and be guided by foreigners in order to have any hope of catching up with them. Conversely, many government organizations employ foreigners but often cannot use them and are used by them. They do not know that although foreigners are better than us, they do not speak Chinese and do not know the needs of China. Without a competent Chinese leader to direct them, not only will they not be able to use their talents to the fullest, but they will also cause problems. Moreover, although most foreign scientists are better than us, few of them are able to guide us and are also willing to come to China. The foreigners employed by the Geological Survey are all first-class talents who cooperate with their Chinese colleagues under the direction of the leaders, so they are able to achieve considerable results.

Although the above-mentioned conditions are important, without a director who is willing to sacrifice himself, the Geological Survey would certainly not have achieved its current success. During the most difficult times for the Geological Survey, from the fourteenth year of the Republic (1925) to the sixteenth year of the Republic (1927), Mr. Weng Wenhao did not take any salary at all. Twenty-three years ago, the director was a recommended official, but Mr. Weng was unwilling to leave the Geological Survey, so he was unwilling to become the president of Tsinghua University and the Minister of Education. Currently, the director has been changed to a simplified appointment official, but Mr. Weng is taking the lowest salary of a simplified appointment official. This kind of spirit has naturally spread to the hearts of all the employees of the institute. Many people would rather take less salary than be willing to leave the Geological Survey. Those who do fieldwork consider enduring hardship and taking risks as extremely ordinary things. In the eighteenth year of the Republic (1929), Mr. Zhao Yahui was dispatched to Sichuan and Yunnan. He would rather be killed by bandits in Zhaotong than give up the original investigation plan. In the winter of the nineteenth year of the Republic (1930), Mr. Wang Hengsheng was arrested by Russian troops on the border of Heilongjiang as a spy and imprisoned in a Siberian prison, drinking cold water and eating black bread for eighteen days, almost being shot twice. After he was released, when he arrived in Manzhouli, he continued to do his fieldwork as usual. He did not return until the planned plan was implemented. This kind of spirit is the foundation of our nation's revival. I hope that every young person knows these facts and learns from their example.

The scientific research organization that was established after the Geological Survey was the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China. The Science Society of China was organized by Chinese students studying in the United States in the fourth year of the Republic (1915) and established in Ithaca, New York. In the seventh year of the Republic (1918), the operating organization moved from the United States to China. At that time, the business was to compile and print a popular magazine called "Science." In the ninth year of the Republic (1920), Mr. Bing Zhi returned from the United States to serve as a professor of zoology at Southeast University. Mr. Bing was one of the founders of the Science Society and one of the first directors. He was the most enthusiastic researcher, but Southeast University was originally a higher normal school, and not only were the equipment and facilities very simple, the buildings were very small, but also the teaching was very heavy, and the authorities did not have the ability to promote research work. Therefore, Mr. Bing wanted to use the Science Society as a base for studying biology. Coincidentally, the Ministry of Finance allocated the official property in Wende Lane, Chengxian Street, Nanjing to the Science Society for its office. In addition to offices and libraries, there were also a few remaining houses. Mr. Bing, together with his friend Mr. Hu Xiansiu, a professor of botany at Southeast University, proposed to organize a biological research institute within the Science Society. It was established in the eleventh year of the Republic (1922), with Mr. Bing as the director and Mr. Hu as a researcher. At that time, the Biological Research Institute only occupied two small houses, and the annual funding was only 240 yuan! Mr. Bing and Mr. Hu not only did not receive salaries, but also, together with their friends Mr. Chen Huanxi and Mr. Chen Zhen, each took out their own books and placed them in the Science Society as a public library. The necessary instruments and medicines were borrowed from Southeast University. During the day, they were busy teaching and had no time, so they ran to the institute after dinner in the evening to work. In the twelfth year of the Republic (1923), they obtained two more larger rooms from the Science Society to serve as display rooms. In the autumn of this year, the Jiangsu Provincial Government decided to subsidize them with 300 yuan per month. From the twelfth year to the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926), the total annual funding for the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society was only 3,840 yuan, but Mr. Bing and his friends separately took charge of various tasks such as collection, display, and research, and published eight papers one after another. Their work was done at night and in the summer, because they were busy teaching at other times. I still remember that in the summer of the thirteenth year of the Republic (1924), the Science Society held its tenth anniversary conference at the Nanjing Institute. The weather was extremely hot that day, and it was impossible to sit in the house, so all the procedures of the meeting were held in the open air. After dinner, various games and entertainment were held. I looked everywhere for Mr. Bing but could not see his shadow. Later, I learned that he and his assistants were hidden upstairs holding their microscopes! Soon, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War broke out, and Nanjing was repeatedly panicked, but Mr. Bing and his colleagues not only did not move their homes to escape, but also worked as usual every day without interruption.

From the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926) until now, the Science Society has received subsidies from the China Education and Culture Foundation, and the funding has gradually become more abundant than before. The first subsidy was 15,000 yuan per year, and currently it is 46,000 yuan, but at most it is only 50,000 yuan. On the one hand, the Biological Research Institute constantly sends people to collect specimens in the field, and on the other hand, it builds new houses and increases equipment. Now the instruments and display rooms are roughly equipped, and more than 90 papers have been published, with a collection of thousands of books and more than 50,000 specimens. The economy of expenditure can be said to be "worlds apart" from that of general government organizations.

The work of the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society mainly focuses on classification. In recent years, some people have criticized Mr. Bing, thinking that his work is too unfashionable and too narrow. This criticism is unfair. It is true that in European and American countries, the taxonomy of flora and fauna is already outdated. However, this is because they have figured out the types and distribution of the flora and fauna in their own countries over the past two hundred years. It is not that taxonomy is unimportant. We have just begun. For example, nothing is more practical than fisheries, agriculture, and forestry in terms of its relationship with flora and fauna. If we cannot even explain how many kinds of fish, trees, or pests there are, how can we talk about application or advanced studies? Mr. Bing's work in classification is a sacrifice for him personally, because he originally studied morphology, and his personal interest was not in classification. The scope of botany and zoology is too broad. It is impossible to include all kinds of research work in one organization. What's more, his funding is only 46,000 yuan per year!

I have already said at the beginning that the number of research organizations in China is gradually increasing. The reason why I only talk about the Geological Survey and the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society is that, firstly, there is not enough time, and secondly, I personally know these two organizations particularly clearly, especially since both of them have gone through difficult and arduous creation. I am not "flaunting" my friends, their achievements are there, and they do not need anyone to flaunt them. I want to let ambitious young people know these facts and be inspired by them. I often say to middle-aged people: Modern young people are better than us. I also want to say to young people: Society is not completely evil, and the spirit of a few seniors in doing things and learning is enough to be a model for young people.

Real Department: Adjusting Mining Finance

More Than a Dozen Cases Approved; Total Amount Estimated at 5 Million Yuan

According to the Central News Agency, the Ministry of Industry has established a Mining Finance Adjustment Committee to handle 10 million yuan in commercial loans. The aim is to adjust the economic conditions of various mines, supervise improvements in their operations, and promote development. It is reported that many mines have requested loans. The committee has investigated and verified a dozen cases, which have been submitted to the Ministry for approval. The total amount of the loans is approximately 5 million yuan. The loan contracts have already been drafted and will be formally signed and submitted to the Ministry after the respective mines convene shareholder meetings and pass the resolutions. The Ministry will guarantee the repayment of principal and interest. The remaining mines are still under investigation. According to the person in charge of the committee, the collateral for the loans is the assets of the mines, with the Ministry of Industry as the guarantor. The Ministry will be responsible for repaying the principal and interest to the banking syndicate. Therefore, the committee, acting as a representative of the Ministry, will supervise the operations of the mines at any time. If a mine fails due to business failure and cannot repay the loan, the Ministry has the right to take over the mine's assets for reorganization and development. Although such provisions exist for the loans, the investigation and review processes are quite strict, so it is unlikely that such a situation will occur.

Sichuan Finance and Construction Commissioners: Flew to Sichuan Together Yesterday Morning; Liu Discussed the Success of the 12 Million Yuan Loan; Lu Said the Date of Assuming the Construction Commissioner Position is Undecided

According to the Guowen News Agency, Liu Hangchen, the Finance Commissioner of Sichuan Province and Deputy Director of the Finance Supervisory Office of the Military Affairs Commission, and Lu Zuofu, the Construction Commissioner and General Manager of Minsheng Industrial Company, recently flew to Shanghai for official business. They completed their tasks and took the China National Aviation Corporation's westward plane together at 7:00 AM yesterday morning, flying directly to Chongqing. Before departing, Liu told a reporter from the Guowen News Agency that Sichuan's finances have gradually improved since the central government decided to rectify them. The previous situation of spending without revenue has been completely reversed. All 60 million yuan of local banknotes issued by various armies and banks in the past, except for half of which had cash reserves, the remaining 30 million yuan were completely recovered by the Central Bank at 80% of their face value. After the deadline of November 15th, all local banknotes have completely disappeared from the market. This has led to a significant shortage of currency. At the same time, the volume of transactions is large, but the Central Bank's banknotes only amount to 24 million yuan, which is definitely not enough to meet the needs of circulation throughout Sichuan. Therefore, the financial community in Chongqing, on the one hand, plans to use a type of remittance certificate as a substitute for cash in Chongqing (totaling approximately 9 million yuan), and on the other hand, plans to apply to the Ministry of Finance to issue 35 million yuan in banknotes, with 60% cash and 40% guarantee reserves. Unexpectedly, after the Ministry of Finance announced the nationalization of silver on November 4th and implemented the new monetary policy, this banknote issuance plan was tacitly abandoned. However, the problem of currency shortage still needs to be resolved with a good solution. Therefore, I specifically flew to Shanghai a few days ago with Guan Jiyu, the Director of the Finance Supervisory Office of the Military Affairs Commission, and Kang Xinru, the General Manager of Sichuan Meifeng Bank (representing the financial community in Chongqing), to consult with Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi. We have now obtained the approval of Minister Kong to use the 70 million yuan of Sichuan Rehabilitation Bonds issued by the government as collateral. In addition to the original 4 million yuan temporarily postponed for repayment, an additional 8 million yuan will be borrowed, totaling 12 million yuan. Four million yuan will be lent to the financial community in Chongqing, and 4 million yuan will be lent to the Sichuan reconstruction financial authorities for the purpose of recovering the remittance certificates circulating in Chongqing that are not redeemable. After I return to Sichuan, the Chongqing branch of the Central Bank can allocate the funds to alleviate the current difficulties. As for the fundamental solution in the future, we should take our time to plan it. Roughly speaking, we hope that the Central Bank can handle commodity mortgage and bill discounting, etc. Currently, Sichuan's tax revenue is approximately 6.9 million yuan per year, and expenditures are approximately 6.4 million yuan. Although this is the first time that the Sichuan Provincial Government has had a preliminary budget since its establishment, it is quite difficult to balance revenue and expenditure given the years of war, fires, and impoverishment of the people and finances in Sichuan, and the need to address various problems. As for the future of Sichuan's finances, first, it depends on whether the common disaster in Sichuan can be eliminated, and further, how to stabilize the people's lives. Second, it depends on the international situation and the changes in Shanghai's financial circles. If there are no problems with these two items, then it is very optimistic. Sichuan is rich in resources, but it lacks large amounts of capital for development and means to transport goods out of the province. We hope that Shanghai's financial community can invest more in construction. If managed properly, Sichuan is the most promising province. When the reporter spoke with Liu, Lu was in the room. He replied that he was busy with company management and had limited knowledge, so he could not take on this important task. He had already submitted his resignation, but Chairman Liu repeatedly urged and exhorted him to reluctantly accept. He was in a dilemma and agreed to consider it further. Therefore, the date of assuming the position is temporarily uncertain. He will make a decision after returning to Sichuan and consulting with Chairman Liu.

Cai Zengji Discusses with Various Parties: Reorganizing the Land System

Cai Zengji, the Director of the Land Bureau of this city, has openly discussed the issue of reorganizing the land system in Shanghai, gathering ideas from various parties, hoping to make the system perfect. Recently, various parties have published opinions in the North China Daily News. Director Cai has discussed them in detail. As this newspaper believes that this matter concerns social issues, it has translated and described Director Cai's original text published in the North China Daily News as follows: On the 29th of last month, a gentleman published an opinion on the issue of land mortgage in the North China Daily News, advocating that the mortgagee must have direct and clear auction rights. His statement is very good. However, the draft proposal for the reform of land property mortgage suggested by this Bureau already contains this meaning in the section on the execution of mortgage rights. According to Article 2 of the proposed draft, it is clearly stipulated that "If the mortgagee has not received payment after the debt maturity date and has been approved to notify the mortgagor to proceed, and still has not made payment, he may directly hand it over to a well-known auction house in this city to execute the auction." This means that the auction can be carried out without the intervention of the court first. The court will only deal with the matter when new evidence of land ownership is discovered, causing disputes in the auction or mortgage. Even if the mortgage is handled in accordance with English law (English law advocates that the mortgagee has direct and clear auction rights), if there is a dispute and the defendant is Chinese, the handling of the dispute cannot be separated from Chinese law and Chinese courts. Article 873 of the Civil Code stipulates that "Any agreement stipulating that the ownership of the mortgaged property shall be transferred to the mortgagee when the debt maturity date has arrived and payment has not been made is invalid." Therefore, according to the current Chinese law, the Chinese people cannot privately enter into a mortgage contract and naturally transfer the ownership of the mortgaged property to the mortgagee. Even if Chinese law does not have this explicit provision, in terms of general law, according to international law and common customs, it has never allowed the people of a country to voluntarily waive their domestic laws and their protection. For example, British people in their own country cannot voluntarily waive the rights granted and enjoyed by British law and turn to Chinese law. This is clear evidence. Therefore, when a Chinese is the defendant, the case must be handled by a Chinese court and judged by Chinese law. The perpetual lease system (rather than trust deed) in which foreigners register in consulates and practice on behalf of nationals is unique to other countries. Under this system, cunning people often use illegal methods to steal deeds and implement mortgages, which is undeniable. The proposed plan can reduce these illegal events. Therefore, although the mortgagee and mortgagor have to go through a few more procedures and pay a little more fees, they would like to adopt it. Some say that if this proposal is implemented, the perpetual lease system may be hindered. This statement seems to be overly pessimistic. In fact, the gist of the proposal is sufficient to eliminate existing weaknesses and prevent registered owners and original owners from being estranged again. The perpetual lease system is actually benefited. If the registered owner is also the original owner, the matter is simple. The real right based on the perpetual lease has been fully demonstrated in law. The holder is the owner, and there is no dispute over the issue of real rights. The Bureau's plan is to improve the current laws and procedures regarding the execution of mortgage rights, but its fundamental purpose is to protect the interests of both the mortgagee and mortgagor. Although some say that mortgagees generally know how to protect their own interests, in reality, as stated in the previous article, it is difficult to talk about it easily. What the Bureau is currently formulating is only an outline. As for the detailed items and chapters, such as the fee collection, (the fee collection should be based on the workload), it should be further regulated in detail. As for how the mortgagee should execute legal rights, manage the land, collect rents, and various related procedures and provisions when the mortgagor fails to pay interest, they must be drafted separately when the proposal is decided and promulgated. The land system of this city is waiting to be rebuilt. There is no need to decorate it. To seek a fair and perfect system to protect property rights and end litigation, it is necessary to take time to carefully study it before hastily saying that it is perfect.

In view of the inconvenience of transportation and the poverty of Lingtai, he requested to prepare some sugar, food, and fruits, and quickly hand them over to the plane to be dropped from the sky when it flew over the accident site in Lingtai to meet the needs of the passengers for recuperation. As for the cause of the accident, the telegram stated that it still needs a detailed study of the local situation for a considerable period of time, and will be telegraphed after obtaining the main points. The company has prepared sugar, food, and fruits and handed them over to the westward plane yesterday to be delivered, and sent telegrams to the two passengers to express condolences. The text of the telegram is as follows: "Telegram to President Ma Yusan and County Chief Guo Hanqing, passengers of plane No. 5 dropped by the plane. It is regrettable that our company suffered a natural disaster and the plane crashed, causing harm to you. In addition to dispatching engineers and hiring doctors to rescue and assist, we hereby send some sugar, food, and fruits by special plane to express our sincere condolences and wish you a speedy recovery. Li Jingcong, General Manager of Eurasia Aviation Company."

Chuanshan Steamboat Encountered Danger

Lost Propeller Yesterday Morning in Tongshan Waters; Company Dispatched Tugboat for Assistance, Expected to Arrive Tonight

The Chuanshan steamboat of the Chuanshan Steamboat Company departs from Shanghai every Wednesday to Chuanshan first, and then to Shipu and Haimen for export. The ship left Shanghai with cargo and passengers fully loaded last night. At 4:00 AM yesterday morning, when the ship arrived at the Tongsha waters outside the Wusongkou, the engine propeller suddenly fell off, and the ship could not move. However, due to the lack of radio equipment and the strong wind and waves on the sea, just as it was at a loss, the Ningbo liner Xinjiangtian of China Merchants Bureau happened to pass by the Tongsha waters. At that time, the Chuanshan steamboat had already anchored and waited for rescue. It asked Xinjiangtian to send a radio telegram to Shanghai to report to the company. The original telegram stated briefly that Chuanshan had lost its propeller in the Tongsha waters and was anchored waiting for rescue, and asked the company to send a tugboat to tow it to Shanghai, etc. The company first used the telephone to notify the China Ship Insurance Joint Association and discussed how to tow it. After consultation, it was decided to hire a large tugboat from Jardine Matheson & Co., which left Shanghai yesterday to tow the ship and tow it back to Shanghai. It is expected to arrive at the port after 12:00 PM last night. After unloading the cargo and passengers, it will be docked for repairs and another propeller will be fitted. When the ship arrives in Shanghai, the Chuanshan Company will submit a request to the Navigation Administration Bureau and the Insurance Joint Association to send technicians to inspect the cause of the accident. The detailed report will be made by the shipowner after arriving in Shanghai. The extent of other damage to the ship is not yet known. It is verified that the Chuanshan steamboat is made of iron, with a gross tonnage of 1,040 tons, a registered tonnage of 6,378 tons, a length of 169 feet, a width of 27 feet 8 inches, a depth of 12 feet, a draft of 9 feet, two decks, a triple-expansion engine, 600 horsepower, a steam pressure of 180, and a speed of 11 knots per hour. It was built in Shanghai in 1920. The hull is insured for peace of mind in the China Maritime Insurance Joint Association.

Current Situation of National Goods Industry

Prices of Many Goods Have Increased, but Enameled Porcelain, etc., Have Not Increased in Price; Volume of National Goods Shipped to Nanyang Area Increases Month by Month

According to the Central News Agency, the recent operating conditions of the national goods industry have attracted much attention from various people. A Central News Agency reporter visited Pan Yangyao, who is familiar with the national goods industry, at the Four Banks Joint Treasury, who gave a very detailed account of the industry's situation, which is recorded as follows:

Smaller Factories Cannot Cooperate Since Last Month The national goods industry has seen a slight stagnation in sales due to the soaring prices of raw materials. Because some of the raw materials for national goods are imported, prices have soared, averaging 20%. The price of metals has even risen to one-third of the original price. With the cost of goods high, the purchase price will naturally also rise. At a time when purchasing power is weak, sales are stagnant, and stockpiles accumulate, capital cannot circulate. Selling at low prices again results in capital losses. Therefore, the current situation is somewhat difficult, and the industry cannot cooperate and competes with each other. Recently, national goods factories with extremely small capital have been found on the market, making crude products and selling them cheaply, which has further weakened the sales of goods from various manufacturers. However, larger manufacturers have clearly understood the necessity of cooperation and many are proceeding with cooperation.

Foreign Merchants Plan to Establish Factories in the Mainland The most difficult aspect of the future of the national goods industry is the planning of foreign merchants to establish factories in the mainland of China. After the Ministry of Finance revised the import and export tariff rates, the import tariff rates for some goods increased significantly. Foreign merchants felt that the promotion of goods in China was affected, so they planned to establish factories in the mainland of China to produce and sell goods, which would be more profitable. This plan is currently underway. If it is realized one day, the production and sales of the national goods industry will inevitably be greatly affected, so the national goods industry is extremely concerned about this.

Promoting National Goods in Various Overseas Regions After the price of raw materials for national goods soared, the prices of many goods increased due to cost factors, but the prices of some goods, such as enameled porcelain, etc., did not increase, so sales have been very strong recently. National goods manufacturers have recently increased their recruitment of personnel for sales and have been promoting sales in the interior, and large quantities of goods have been continuously shipped to even the remote provinces with inconvenient transportation. Overseas regions have also gradually been developed, and the volume of national goods shipped to the Nanyang area has been increasing month by month, which is a good sign.

More Than 1,000 Overseas Chinese in Siam Detained for Failing to Pay Political Assistance Fee

Overseas Chinese in Siam are required to pay a political assistance fee of six baht to the resident government every year. This political assistance fee is also known as a poll tax or head tax. After paying, Chinese people must carry the receipt with them, because the police have the right to check it at any time. If they do not have this receipt, they will be punished with hard labor or detention. Last month was the period for collecting political assistance fees for young people. Because the Siamese government has been rejecting Chinese workers and employing Siamese workers in recent years, unemployment is everywhere. Even food and clothing cannot be maintained, so where can there be surplus funds to pay the head tax? Therefore, on the first day after the collection period ended, the Siamese police began to inspect. Within three hours, the number of Chinese who had not paid the political assistance fee reached more than 1,000. After being arrested, they were all detained at the police school. As of the reporter's press time, no accurate information has been received as to how to deal with them.

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent letters to the Chemical Raw Materials, Fireworks, Rubber Products, Pickled and Preserved Products, Enamel, Machinery and Dyeing, and Medicinal Materials Associations, as well as the China Chemical Industry Society, the Great China Match Company, and other stores and members, stating that on the 4th of this month, they received a letter from the Jiangsu Provincial Nitre and Sulfur General Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, Su Zi No. 429, stating that "In the case of the Ministry of Finance's order Jian Zi No. 19549 issued on October 19 of this year, it was found that the deadline for submitting nitre and sulfur forms for cancellation has been stated by oneself. If any have exceeded the cancellation deadline and have not yet been submitted, they will be urged to submit them quickly and must not be negligent. At the end of each month, the submitted forms will be verified and forwarded to the ministry for separate storage and verification for cancellation. In addition to separate orders, it is hereby ordered to comply," and so on. In view of this, it was found that most of the above-mentioned forms requested by various parties have a deadline for cancellation, but many have not been submitted after the deadline. The Municipal Land Bureau Implements the Method of Photographing and Filing Single Deeds

In order to allow people to retrieve their single deeds for safekeeping after exchanging certificates, the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau previously drafted a method of photographing and filing deeds, which was published in the newspapers on November 24. It is now learned that the method has been approved by the Municipal Government and will be implemented from the 2nd of this month. Anyone who submits a single deed or other important evidence for verification when exchanging a Gui Di practice certificate, which is not related to the retention of the Land Bureau, may apply for photography at the Receiving and Dispatching Office. The Fourth Section of the Land Bureau will verify, stamp, and number the single deed, and after waiting for the photograph, the item can be taken and submitted. After the Fourth Section compares it with the original single deed and confirms that there are no errors, it will be returned. The procedure is very convenient, and the photography price is also very low. It is heard that after the implementation of this method, all owners can retrieve their single deeds for dealing with other disputes during the certificate exchange period, which is very convenient.

The Weather in This Port Turns Clear; Heavy Fog Yesterday Morning; Ships and Airplanes Were Delayed

After the snowfall in this port the day before yesterday, there were intermittent rain showers in the evening. Yesterday, it was late in clearing up. Although the weather had turned clear and cold, the fog was extremely heavy, especially between 7:00 and 8:00 a.m. The visibility was unclear beyond a few steps. The vehicles on the streets had to reduce their speed and move slowly. The shops also opened and burned electric lights for business. The China Aviation Company's Shanghai-Hankou-West aircraft was also delayed from 7:00 a.m. to 8:35 a.m. The Shanghai-Ping Beijing-bound aircraft was also delayed.

Land Owners in the City Center Request Cancellation of Fallow Land Donation; Economic Downturn Prevents Merchants from Investing

According to Shen Shi News Agency, in order to complete the Greater Shanghai Plan, the Shanghai Municipal Government has divided the land in the city center into phases for recruitment, limiting the time for building city houses. The Construction Committee of the Municipal Government has also built sports fields, municipal libraries, swimming pools, and dormitories, cooperatives, etc. for the staff of the Municipal Government's various branch bureaus in the city center as an example of promotion. Banks in the city have also built new villages there, which have been completed one after another. The Municipal Government, in view of the fact that some of the land obtained by the owners has not yet been reported for construction, which has hindered the completion of Greater Shanghai, has approved a time limit for construction to make the plan to prosper Greater Shanghai a reality as soon as possible. Otherwise, a fallow land donation will be collected. The Land Owners Association in the City Center believes that this kind of donation method is not found in the major cities of our country. Moreover, during this extremely depressed period, merchants are unable to invest, which is also reasonable. Moreover, due to economic panic, the special zone owners have many empty lots and cannot build. The special zone authorities do not have any regulations limiting construction. If this precedent is set, what are the consequences? Therefore, at 4:00 p.m. the other day, the association convened an emergency meeting of all land owners at the association's office on Beijing Road to discuss countermeasures. Dozens of people, including Li Bohan and Xi Yanfang, attended. Everyone believed that this kind of donation method for fallow land was not found in the major cities of the country, and Shanghai should not set this precedent. This kind of donation tax is difficult for the association to recognize. A resolution was passed on the spot to jointly petition the Municipal Government authorities to sympathize with the difficulties of the merchants and cancel it. If the city's economy turns around, they will invest and build according to the construction procedures.

Japanese Consulate Police Station Intercepts a Large Batch of Silver

Totaling 22,455 Yuan

According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily, at 9:00 a.m. yesterday (5th), when the Japanese ship Nagasaki Maru was about to depart, Police Chief Fukuyama of the Japanese Consulate Police Station, led Patrol Chief Matsuo and Detective Higuchi, etc., to inspect the secret transportation of silver at the Huishan Pier, but unexpectedly intercepted 21 secret transporters, with silver amounting to 22,455 yuan. In addition to being found in luggage, many of the guests who were seeing them off also secretly carried it on their bodies, and it was searched out one by one. According to the North China Daily News, when a certain Japanese ship arrived in Shanghai on Wednesday, it carried more than 500 Japanese passengers in third class. The ship had changed its usual route in order to transport this type of passenger to Nagasaki, so it arrived a day later than scheduled. After arriving in Shanghai, most of these passengers were engaged in the trafficking of silver dollars. Although the Shanghai Japanese Consulate Police, in cooperation with the Chinese Customs, strictly prohibit the private export of silver, this news has apparently not yet spread to the villages around Nagasaki. Many Japanese who deliberately try to buy silver privately in Shanghai come from that area. Of the 500 people who arrived in Shanghai on Wednesday, it is likely that more than half will return disappointed. According to shipping company sources, the number of third-class passengers traveling between Shanghai and Nagasaki in the middle of last month was three times higher than usual. A certain company, which averages one ship arriving in Shanghai every four days, told the North China Daily News yesterday that each time it carries between 150 and 200 Japanese passengers who appear to be small traders, and the third-class seats are fully booked when departing from Shanghai to Nagasaki. It is not known why these people are so busy.

The radio stations and broadcasting frequencies are listed below: Overseas Chinese XMHC (700 kHz), Buddhist Voice XMHB (980 kHz), China-America XMHA (600 kHz), Qikai XQHB (820 kHz), Jianhua XHHB (740 kHz).

Public Concession Real Estate Tax Assessment - Municipal Council Issues Official Statement

Original Tax Policy Unchanged - Separate Valuation for Tax Limited to Special Circumstances - Responding to Principles Proposed by Chinese Taxpayers - No Dispute over the Legal Status of the Property Valuation Committee

The Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association published an article on October 30th regarding the Municipal Council's rental assessment and tax collection methods, which was widely reported in the local newspapers. The main point of the article was that the Municipal Council had abandoned its established practice of levying property taxes based on the rental amounts listed on property deeds and had instead adopted a method of assessing taxes based on estimated property values. The Municipal Council authorities took this matter very seriously and issued an important statement, earnestly declaring to taxpayers that the Municipal Council's original property tax policy had not been changed or amended. The basis for assessing taxes based on estimated values is the same today as it was 65 years ago. In order to ensure a balanced tax burden, the Municipal Council has the right to estimate rental values. The initial basis for this right is the Land Regulations of 1854. Furthermore, estimated values are applied to both self-owned and rented properties, without any doubt. The Municipal Council operates on the principle that while rental amounts can serve as documentary evidence of a property's taxable value, they are sometimes insufficient. Since 1867, various courts have repeatedly reviewed this point and confirmed its validity, stating in their judgments, "After careful review of the arguments presented by both sides, we are firmly convinced that the Municipal Council has the right to estimate rental values separately from the actual rent for the purpose of levying taxes." Of course, the most appropriate and widely applicable basis for distributing taxes in a given area is the rented property. Therefore, the type of property is examined and flexible standards are established so that the amount of tax can automatically adjust according to the property's value, in order to achieve balance. The soundness of this approach is universally recognized and needs no further elaboration. However, since the goal of taxation in a given area is to balance the burden on the general public, the rental price of a property must be fairly compared to other properties. Can a single property deed be considered a perfectly fair and unbiased standard? Therefore, the Municipal Council of the Public Concession uses the annual rental value of each property as the standard for assessing municipal general rates. For these properties, the property owner has no other obligations besides external repairs, and the documentary value of the property deed is considered by the Municipal Council to adequately represent the rental value, and is used as the standard for levying general rates in the vast majority of cases. However, as mentioned above, when the property deed is insufficient, the Municipal Council must estimate the rental value in order to balance the burden on the public, using the same type of property in the same area as the standard to calculate the appropriate tax. However, this type of event only accounts for a tiny minority of all properties in the Concession, which is the point of contention for the Chinese Taxpayers Association. The following is a list of cases where the property deed is insufficient:

(1) When the rent is reduced due to business connections or familial ties between the property owner and the tenant.

(2) When the tenant originally rented the property at a fair price, but later made permanent improvements and additions, significantly increasing the property's rental value.

(3) When the tenant does not pay the full rent, but instead provides partial compensation in the form of cash. In this case, the actual rent should be calculated by adding the face value of the rent to the total annual cash compensation.

(4) When, apart from economic reasons, the property owner waives a portion of the rent because the tenant is an employee of the property owner or indirectly provides services to the property owner.

(5) When the property owner and the tenant collude to forge property deeds in order to evade general rates.

From these various cases, it can be seen that the Municipal Council has no choice but to use a comparative method as the basis for taxation when the property deed amount differs significantly from the property's value. This method is also essential for protecting the interests of the majority of taxpayers, as the general public has already paid the full amount of taxes on the actual rental value of their properties.

Furthermore, as the Chinese Taxpayers Association stated in its opinion, "The Municipal Council is using outdated provisions of the Land Regulations to effectively increase tax revenue," and, "For example, if the rent is 100 yuan and the tax rate is 14%, the monthly tax should be 14 yuan. If the value is overestimated to 150 yuan, the total tax will be 21 yuan. This does not increase the tax rate, but the total tax increases by one and a half times, equivalent to increasing the tax rate from 14% to 21%." The Municipal Council must correct this point: if someone presents a property deed showing a monthly rent of 100 yuan, but the property's actual rental value is known to be 150 yuan per month, and the Municipal Council allows them to pay tax based on 100 yuan, then the tax rate they pay will be less than 14%, only 9.33%. The unpaid tax will inevitably be distributed among other taxpayers who pay according to the regulations, which is unfair in both law and reason.

From this, it can be seen that the Chinese Taxpayers Association's statement that the Municipal Council has abandoned its practice of using the rental amount listed on the property deed as the basis for tax collection and has instead adopted a method of assessing taxes based on estimated values is a misunderstanding. The Municipal Council has not abandoned or changed its tax principles or established practices. In recent years, the Municipal Council has only been more precise in auditing and investigating the rents declared by tenants, making it difficult for a small number of scheming individuals in society to achieve their selfish desires.

Furthermore, the method of collecting property taxes in the Shanghai Municipal Government's administrative area outside the Public Concession is the same as the above. Article 10 of the Shanghai Municipal Property Tax Collection Regulations states: "The determination of the rental value shall be based on the property deed or rental agreement for the most recent two months. If there is a significant discrepancy between the property and the rental value, the rental value shall be separately assessed for the purpose of collecting property taxes. For self-owned properties occupied by the owner, the Finance Bureau shall send personnel to assess the value. If there is a dispute over the assessed rental value, the Property Valuation Committee shall evaluate it." (See the Shanghai Municipal Government Gazette of October 10, 1934). The aforementioned Valuation Committee is composed of six officials from various bureaus of the Municipal Government and three members of a Municipal Government committee. Here are simple answers to the three principles proposed in the Chinese Taxpayers Association's opinion:

Principle 1: "The Municipal Council should levy taxes based on the actual rent for properties with actual rents. For properties owned and occupied by the owner, taxes may be levied based on the estimated rent." If this principle is applied, it may hinder the balance of taxation and contradict court decisions.

Principle 2: "The Municipal Council's establishment of the so-called Property Valuation Committee has no legal basis. Its judgments have no binding force on the outside world." The right to assess taxes based on estimated values belongs to the Municipal Council, but the Council is not a technical body and must hire specialists as consultants. Therefore, the Council does not dispute the legal status of the committee.

Principle 3: "The Municipal Council may not arbitrarily increase taxes. Unless taxpayers agree to change the tax rate, taxpayers have the absolute right to refuse to pay taxes increased by the Municipal Council outside the law." While the right to set the tax rate rests with the taxpayers, the Municipal Council's duty is to strive for a balanced distribution of taxes. The result of this method is to reduce the average burden on taxpayers, not to increase it.

Wang Changlin Sued by Adoptive Mother, Trial Concluded

Adoptive Mother Brings Ancestral Tablet to Court to Prove Changlin is Indeed Adopted Son

—Debate Concluded Yesterday, Date Set for Pronouncement—

Wang Changlin, currently an assistant manager at a certain bank, was adopted at the age of fourteen by his widowed aunt, Mrs. Wang Shi, because her husband died without offspring. Mrs. Wang Shi possessed a large inheritance and devoted herself to nurturing Changlin, hoping to bring honor to the family. She provided him with a thorough education. After graduating from Tsinghua University in Beiping, she continued to provide funds for him to study in America. She also provided financial assistance to Changlin's biological mother from time to time, sparing no expense even if it meant depleting her own wealth. Unexpectedly, Changlin's biological parents suddenly published a notice when their son was about to return home, declaring the cancellation of the adoption agreement. When Changlin returned to Shanghai, he was not allowed to meet with his adoptive mother. By this time, Mrs. Wang Shi had become a poor old woman. Seeing Changlin return home in glory, working in the financial sector and earning hundreds of dollars a month, she thought that even animals know how to repay their parents. She negotiated with him, asking for support. Changlin could not shirk his responsibility and initially agreed to pay 40 dollars a month, but each payment was delayed in various ways, causing Mrs. Wang Shi extreme hardship in recent times. Unable to endure it any longer, she hired lawyer Wang Liwu to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court against Wang Changlin to confirm their mother-son relationship, requesting the court to order the defendant to pay 100 dollars per month for living expenses and to repay the 5,000 dollars previously advanced for tuition. A summons had already been issued, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Yuhai opened the court and continued the trial. Both parties and witnesses appeared in court as summoned. The plaintiff, Mrs. Wang Shi, was already in her sixties, with white hair. To prove the fact of Changlin's adoption, she brought to the court her late husband's ancestral tablet made in 1918. The tablet bore the words "Also Adopted Son Wang Changlin." The old woman's eyes were blurred, and she shed tears as she gazed at the tablet. First, witness Mrs. Xi Shi testified that Wang Changlin's monthly payment of 40 dollars to the plaintiff was initially delivered through her third sister. After her third sister died, Changlin occasionally sent it to her house through someone else. Next, the plaintiff, Mrs. Wang Shi, stated that the defendant returned to the country in 1926 and handed over all the family property to him for management in 1929, which was all squandered. Now the defendant lives in a foreign-style house and rides in a car, while I live in a rented small room and struggle to make ends meet, pawning items to survive. She then presented a large bundle of pawn tickets, estimated to be worth over a thousand dollars. The defendant, Wang Changlin, testified that he was an assistant manager at a certain bank, earning a monthly salary of over 320 dollars, and claimed that the plaintiff's family property was squandered by the plaintiff herself. The court stated that the defendant, as a junior member of the family, should not disregard the livelihood of his elders and engage in litigation. After reprimanding the defendant, the lawyers for both sides debated each other to a conclusion, then were ordered to withdraw and await the verdict.

General Situation of Shanghai Cotton Cloth Industry (Continued)

Compiled by China Credit Information Service

(No. 4 of General Survey of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

6. Sales Situation

Shanghai is the largest cotton cloth market in our country. The sales of cotton cloth extend to all parts of the country and the Nanyang region. Those engaged in this industry are divided into two types: Zihao (firms) and Menzhuang (shops). Zihao mainly engage in wholesale, while Menzhuang mainly engage in retail. Some operate independently, while others operate jointly. During the heyday of this industry (1929 to 1931), there were about a thousand large and small shops. The total annual turnover reached about 100 million yuan or more. After 1932, the Northeast became a purely Japanese goods market. In the provinces of North China, due to the strong presence of Japanese goods in Qingdao, Tianjin, and other ports, only sporadic sales were made. South China, such as Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, and Guizhou provinces, had better sales, but Japanese goods were also quite active. In Sichuan, Jiangxi, and Fujian provinces, after the chaos of bandits, the economy was depressed, and transactions were minimal in the early stages, but have gradually turned around recently. In Hunan and Henan provinces, due to the proliferation of small-scale weaving factories, most areas are self-sufficient. The market conditions in Hubei, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces are sluggish and no longer what they used to be. In the Nanyang region, due to sluggish sales of local products, the amount of goods purchased has sharply decreased. Statistics show that the total sales volume for the whole year is about 50 million yuan (from July 1934 to June 1935), which is only about seven-tenths of the previous year. Transactions on the Inner Bund Street account for about 20 percent, or about 10 million yuan. Sales in South China provinces account for 50 percent, or about 25 million yuan. Sales in North China account for 20 percent, or about 15 million yuan. If we consider the regional location of the shops in this city, the business of those opened in the British and French concessions must be reduced by about 30 percent. Those opened in Hongkou and Nanshi must be reduced by about [blank], and those opened in Zhabei, Pudong, and other places must be reduced by about [blank] of 50.

7. Comparison of Market Prices

Last year, a huge outflow of silver from our country caused a financial panic, and credit became extremely tight. The market was sluggish, so the consumption of cotton cloth decreased sharply compared to the previous year, and market prices trended downwards. Sales were quite slow in the spring and summer seasons. After autumn, transactions gradually became more active, with the Tianjin group purchasing the most. The groups along the two railway lines came in second. Market prices rebounded slightly. However, due to the low purchasing power in the interior, sales soon became sluggish again. Market prices were never able to remain firm. In the first three months of this year, cloth sales remained sluggish, and market prices showed no signs of rebounding. After April, there was a slight turnaround. Wholesale sales to both local and out-of-town merchants were extremely active, especially those to the Ningbo group and along the Yangtze River. Sales were excellent. Market prices were firm. As the end of April approached, credit became tighter, and out-of-town merchants hesitated to move forward. Except for the smooth transactions in Sichuan and Guangdong, the rest were only sporadic additions, with very small quantities. Between May and June, as the summer season arrived, the goods that should have been on the market were already sufficiently stocked in various places, and transactions were quiet. Only the Sichuan and Guangdong groups had slightly stronger transactions. Transactions gradually picked up in July. Sales were good in the local area, Tianjin, Guangdong, and various ports along the Yangtze River. Market prices were stable. Between August and September, various groups added winter goods, and sales were very strong. The coastal merchants along the Yangtze River purchased even more, and business in the local area was also active. Furthermore, as gold prices trended higher and costs increased, the prices of all cotton cloths rose in unison. Some rose by one or two cents, while others rose by several jiao. From October to the present, because gold prices have become increasingly firm, foreign exchange rates have shrunk, and raw materials have become gradually more expensive, cloth prices have also risen with the tide. Furthermore, because the currency is about to be devalued, shops with more financial resources are all hoarding as much as possible, so transactions are extremely busy. However, this type of transaction is purely due to stimulation by monetary policy. If the general purchasing power cannot be increased, the prospects for cotton cloth are still not optimistic. The following table compares the market prices of various major cotton cloths over the past two years.

8. Current Status of the Industry

The cotton cloth industry is extremely important in the Shanghai market. During the heyday of the industry, there were about a thousand large and small businesses in the city. The total annual turnover reached about 100 million yuan or more. In recent years, due to frequent troubles and the people's livelihood being depressed, business has declined year by year. According to statistics released by the Cotton Cloth Industry Association, the total turnover in the past year has decreased to 50 million yuan, only half of that during the heyday. The details are in the following table. (Unit: 1,000 yuan)

Business Type Number of Businesses Capital Annual Turnover

Wholesale 210 2,300 23,000

Retail 250 3,000 17,000

Wholesale and Retail 40 850 10,000

Total 500 6,150 50,000

In the "Domestic Goods" section, the second line, "On average, about 10,000 pieces of white goods per 'day'" should read "On average, about 10,000 pieces of white goods per 'month.'" Furthermore, in the "Japanese Goods" section, the second-to-last line, "The daily output is about 20,000 pieces," should read "The 'monthly' output is about 20,000 pieces." We hope this will be corrected tomorrow! Sincerely,

To the Editor of Shen Bao. From the Documents Department of China Credit Information Service, evening of December 5th.

Yisheng Store Tax Evasion Case, Request to Provide Guarantee and Return Silk, Most of it Certainly Tax Evasion, Customs Obtains Evidence, Request to Provide Guarantee, Court Has Not Yet Approved

Since the tax evasion incident at the Pinzhen Jewelry Store on Nanjing Road, the Jianghai Customs Anti-Smuggling Division has been strictly investigating businesses that evade customs duties and harm the national treasury. Recently, it was found that Yisheng Foreign Goods Store, opened by Liu Mingjia, a native of Huzhou, at 54 Jixian Lane, 195 Tianjin Road, had a large batch of silk that had not paid customs duties. They then requested the First Special District Court to issue a search warrant and, together with Liang Baosheng, a Chinese detective from the Tax Investigation Office of the Public Concession, went to search the premises at 12:30 p.m. on the 25th of last month. Because there was a lot of silk, worth more than 160,000 yuan, it could not be completely confiscated. Only one-quarter of the silk, 272 boxes, as well as account books and other items, were taken back to the police station. The next morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court, which ordered that the seized items be detained and the account books be handed over to the customs for investigation. This has already been reported in this newspaper. Now, Yisheng intends to follow the precedent of Pinzhen by submitting a request to the First Special District Court to allow them to provide a guarantee and have the detained silk returned first. Therefore, yesterday morning, Judge Dai Rongduo opened the Second Criminal Court to investigate whether to allow bail. Liu Mingjia also appeared in court with his attorney, Yu Xiangqin. They stated that the silk seized was worth more than 40,000 yuan when purchased, but is now only worth 27,500 yuan. They requested permission to provide a guarantee and have it returned first. The representative of the Jianghai Customs, Shen Shikun, testified that the account books of Yisheng were difficult to examine because they used an old-fashioned accounting method. In addition to the seized goods, three-quarters of the goods remained at Yisheng, which made the examination slightly more difficult. According to the Customs investigation, most of the goods were tax-evading, except for a small portion that had already paid customs duties. As for Yisheng's request for bail, silk is not the same as pearls. Each piece of silk has a number. If the numbers are switched, the examination will be difficult. The Customs has obtained considerable evidence of its tax evasion and will be able to present it when necessary. The court then inquired about the value of the goods seized by Yisheng, whether it was true, and which articles of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations its actions violated. The Customs representative replied that the Customs has a special department to estimate the value and that he could not answer. However, he was certain that it would not be the amount stated. As for the articles of law violated, they were Articles 21 and 22 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Law. The police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, did not express an opinion on Yisheng's request for bail because the police were only assisting. He requested that the court exercise its own judgment. Judge Dai examined the warrant and stated that Yisheng had not provided sufficient proof of the value of the goods. It should be verified after proof is provided whether or not to approve the guarantee. The court then adjourned, so Yisheng's request for bail is not yet optimistic. Request the court to examine the body.

Chen Renzhao Encountered and Arrested His Runaway Wife on the Road

Chen Renzhao, a native of Xinchang, Zhejiang, is 37 years old and originally farmed in his hometown. His wife, Shi, is 31 years old and was abducted by Shi Changnong, a fellow villager, in September of this year. The Xinchang Local Court of Zhejiang Province arrested Shi and is currently holding him in custody. Chen Renzhao and his friend Ye Zhusan came to Shanghai on business and encountered his wife, Shi, on Bailinan Road in West Shanghai. He immediately grabbed her and reported her to the local sub-station, which transferred her to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Nephew Came to Stay, Used Ax on Cousin

Wu Jinyuan, a farmer in Shiziyuan Township, Caojing District, West Shanghai, had a son, Lin Fu, who farmed at home. At 8:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, his nephew, Shen Heshang, a plasterer from Caobei, Caojiaqiao, Shanghai County, came to his house with an unnamed friend to visit Wu Jinyuan. He thought it was a normal visit from relatives. That night, they stayed in his son's bedroom. In the middle of the night, he suddenly heard cries for help from the room. Jinyuan quickly got up and went to check, but Shen Heshang and the others had fled without a trace. He found that Lin Fu had been slashed in the head with an ax, with a wound about three inches long and half an inch deep behind his left ear. Blood was flowing like a torrent, and he was moaning in pain. An inspection of the room revealed that no clothing or items were missing. He immediately sent the injured man to Shanghai Hospital for diagnosis and treatment and reported the incident to the local police station, requesting that the murderer be arrested and investigated. After receiving the report, Director Wu immediately sent detectives to Shanghai Hospital to inspect the injuries and investigate the truth of the murder. It is now known that Director Wu has not only reported the incident to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, but also sent a letter to the Caojiaqiao Police Sub-station of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau yesterday to assist in the arrest of the murderer Shen Heshang and bring him to justice.

Educational News

Ministry of Education Approves the Regulations of the Liangcai Scholarship Foundation

Donation Fund Totals 160,000 Yuan: Shen Xinqing and Others Serve as Permanent Directors

The Liangcai Scholarship Foundation was established with donations from Mrs. Shi Pang Mingde, wife of the late General Manager Shi Liangcai of this newspaper, and his son Shi Yongdu, etc. Its foundation regulations and list of directors have been submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval. The organizational regulations of the foundation are recorded as follows:

General Principles: Chapter 1 of the Foundation Regulations, General Principles, Article 1: The founders of these regulations, based on the late Mr. Shi Liangcai's wishes, donate 160,000 yuan in national currency as a scholarship fund, establishing a legal entity in accordance with the law, named the Liangcai Scholarship Foundation. Article 2: All 160,000 yuan in national currency belonging to the Foundation will be used as a fund, and its interest will be used to reward academic pursuits in accordance with the provisions of these regulations. Under no circumstances may the principal be used. Article 3: The methods for the Foundation to reward academic pursuits are as follows: (1) Provide scholarships to outstanding high school graduates who are unable to continue their studies due to financial difficulties; (2) Provide tuition assistance to students from public and private universities in the country who are from poor families and have excellent academic records; (3) Provide scholarships to outstanding graduates from universities in the country who wish to study abroad but lack the financial means; (4) Provide research grants to outstanding graduates from universities at home and abroad who specialize in a certain academic field but lack the financial means; (5) Award bonuses to those who have made special inventions or significant contributions in academic fields. Within six years after the establishment of the Foundation, the aforementioned scholarship methods will be limited to those related to natural sciences. Article 4: The Foundation will establish its office within the Shenbao Building on Third Avenue, Shanghai. Branch offices may be established separately when necessary. Chapter 2,

Organization: Article 5: The Foundation will establish a board of directors, composed of eight permanent directors and seven non-permanent directors, representing the Foundation in handling all its affairs. Article 6: Shen Xinqing, Xu Jingren, Chen Taoyi, Qian Xinzhi, Zhang Rongxi, Du Yuesheng, Ma Yinliang, and Shi Yonggeng are nominated as permanent directors, with lifelong terms. If there are any vacancies, they will be filled by the permanent directors jointly. However, no one may be elected as a permanent director without the consent of two-thirds of all permanent directors. With legitimate reasons, a director may resign with the consent of all other permanent directors. Article 7: Non-permanent directors will be jointly elected by the permanent directors from outside the permanent directors, with the consent of more than half of all permanent directors. The term of office is three years, and they may be re-elected upon expiration. Article 8: The board of directors cannot hold a meeting without the presence of more than half of all directors. No resolution can be made without the consent of more than half of the directors present. Article 9: The directors of the Foundation shall elect three people as managing directors to handle all routine affairs on behalf of the board of directors and to convene the board meetings. Article 10: The Foundation will establish a custody committee of three members, elected by the board of directors for a term of three years. The custody committee will jointly manage the Foundation's funds and be responsible for good management. Article 11: In order to deliberate on academic matters, the Foundation may, at any time, invite specialized scholars as review committee members to review events specifically entrusted by the Foundation. Chapter 3

Management: Article 12: In addition to the original 160,000 yuan in national currency, the Foundation shall annually extract a certain amount of interest from the fund to supplement the fund. Those who receive tuition assistance from the Foundation may also include their voluntary return of aid into the fund after they have completed their studies. Article 13: The methods for the custody and utilization of the fund shall be formulated by the custody committee and submitted to the board of directors for resolution. If there are any changes in the future, they must also be resolved by the board of directors first. The management of the fund shall be reported to the directors by the custody committee annually. Article 14: The order and scope of implementation of the scholarship methods stipulated in Article 3 of these regulations shall be determined annually by the board of directors, taking into account financial resources and needs. However, the board of directors may pre-determine an implementation plan for more than one year. Article 15: When the board of directors implements the scholarship methods, it shall formulate detailed implementation rules separately and should consult the opinions of specialized review committee members. Chapter 4

Supplementary Provisions: Article 16: The detailed rules for the board of directors, the detailed rules for the managing directors, the detailed rules for the custody committee, and the detailed rules for the review committee shall be separately determined by the board of directors. Article 17: Matters not covered in these regulations shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of the Civil Code and other laws and regulations regarding legal entities. Article 18: These regulations shall be implemented immediately after being submitted to and approved by the competent authorities and registered. The eight permanent directors are Shen Xinqing, Xu Jingren, Chen Taoyi, Qian Xinzhi, Zhang Rongxi, Du Yuesheng, Ma Yinliang, and Shi Yonggeng. The seven non-permanent directors of the first session are Zhang Yunhe, Huang Renzhi, Hu Bijiang, Wang Xiaolai, Wu Senzhai, Xu Caicheng, and Wang Boqi.

The screening examination for specialist schools and above in this city is scheduled to be held from the 8th to the 10th of this month, with the examination venues divided into three locations: Private Minli, Wuben, and Jingye. The examination schedule has already been arranged and is recorded as follows:

Basic Subjects: Basic subjects, 8th morning, 8:00 AM to 10:00 AM: Chinese (all students), 10:10 AM to 12:10 PM: Foreign Language (all students select), afternoon 1:10 PM to 2:10 PM: Party Principles (all students), 2:20 PM to 3:50 PM: Social Sciences (all students select), 4:00 PM to 5:30 PM: Natural Sciences (all students select). (Note) There are four types of foreign languages: English, French, German, and Japanese. Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Teachers' Association Sends Telegram to the Central Government Requesting an Explicit Order to Suppress the Rebellion

Also Sends Telegram to Song, Shang, and Han Xunyu for Pacifying the Rebellion; Also Sends Telegram to Wang Xiacai Urging Him to Repent

The Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Teachers' Association held an emergency meeting of the board of directors at Zhenjiang Normal School yesterday morning. Huang Boqin, Rong Weisheng, Zhang Tongmo, Wu Cangsu, Wu Zonghan, Zhang Shaonan, and others attended. Huang Boqin presided over the meeting and discussed the following important cases: (1) How should we express our views on Yin's rebellion and betrayal of the country? It was resolved to send a telegram to the central government requesting an explicit order to suppress the rebellion, and to send telegrams to Song Zheyuan, Shang Zhen, and Han Fuju requesting them to suppress the rebellion immediately. (2) How should we express our views on Wang Xiacai's adherence to the rebellion? It was resolved to warn Wang Xiacai and urge him to repent. (3) When will the next representative conference be held? It was decided to hold it on March 11th, 1936, at the Yixing Ceramics Vocational School. The meeting adjourned. The telegrams are recorded as follows:

Telegram to the Central Government: To all members of the Central Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, Chairman Lin of the National Government, Chairman Jiang of the Military Commission, the heads of all the Yuan, and the ministers of all the Bu: As reported, Yin Rugeng is willing to be a puppet, inciting chaos in eastern Hebei, betraying the central government, and endangering the Republic of China. When the news spread, the people of the whole country were outraged. Such a heartless and mad act is a self-inflicted wound to the country and is not allowed by the national law. We request you to issue an explicit order to suppress the rebellion immediately to curb the chaos and maintain the law. Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Teachers' Association respectfully

Telegram to Song and Shang: To Director Song of Beiping Pacification, Chairman Shang of Baoding, and Chairman Han of Jinan: Yin Rugeng is willing to be a puppet, inciting chaos in eastern Hebei and endangering the Republic of China. His crime is unforgivable. We believe that you are known for your public loyalty. Please unite to denounce him and uphold the law to pacify the source of the chaos. The country and the nation depend on it. Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Teachers' Association respectfully

Telegram to the Rebel Wang: As reported, Yin Rugeng is willing to be a puppet, inciting chaos in eastern Hebei. The people of the whole country are outraged. However, you, sir, are also following along and participating. You cannot distinguish between righteousness and profit. There is a way to get rich, why sell your personality to seek it? Moreover, the enemy is insidious and vicious, as the world knows. Once the birds are gone, the bow is put away. Can you, sir, really become rich? Now, Mr. Huo Shi has already refused the rebellious order. What a bright attitude! Truly, the head can be cut off, the family can be destroyed, but a traitor cannot be. What we hope from you, sir, is to rein in the horse at the edge of the cliff and repent. If you insist on going your own way, you will cut yourself off from our Jiangsu and from our country. The world will ask what kind of person you are. As the saying goes, "Condemned by a thousand people, one will die without illness." To be disgraced is not something a wise man would do. We hope you will carefully weigh the advantages and disadvantages of this matter.

Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts Hosts Modern Painting Exhibition in Beijing, Scheduled to Open

Opening Ceremony at the Overseas Chinese Guest House in the Capital on the 8th

The Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts is the source of new and emerging art in our country, and has been engaged in domestic and international art movements for many years, creating a new atmosphere in the domestic art world and arousing great international response. To commemorate the 24th anniversary of the school's founding, a modern painting (Chinese painting and oil painting) exhibition will be held at the Overseas Chinese Guest House in the capital. A preview will be held at 2:00 PM on the 7th to receive leaders from all walks of life for evaluation. The official opening will be on the morning of the 8th, and Chairman Lin will be invited to unveil the exhibition. The collected Chinese and Western paintings have been packed into dozens of boxes and transported to Beijing in advance. The exhibition will close on the 15th. The venue is the Overseas Chinese Guest House on Zhongshan North Road in the capital. The total number of exhibits is more than 460 pieces of Chinese and Western paintings and designs, which is truly a large-scale painting exhibition in the capital in recent days. At that time, the artistic atmosphere of the capital will be greatly invigorated.

Children's Educational Novels

Little Men (116)

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"What you asked me to do, I'm not too worried about—Mother always loves me anyway," replied Rob, now that almost all was lost, he had to cling to the last great support.

"I'm really hungry, let's eat these berries," proposed Dan after a short pause, by which time Rob had begun to doze off.

"I'm hungry too, but I can't eat mine, because I told Mother I would give them all to her."

"You have to eat them, if no one comes to get us," answered Nan, who at this point felt like she had to object to everything. Then she said a few terrible words, "If we stay here for many days, we'll have to eat all the berries in the field, and then we can only wait to die."

"I will eat camphor tree leaves, I know a big yellow camphor tree, Don told me how the squirrels dig up the roots to eat. I love digging too," replied Rob, who was not frightened by the prospect of starving to death.

"That's right; we can catch frogs and cook them. My father ate some, and he said they tasted really good," Nan chimed in, still looking for some adventurous things to do, even though she was lost in the wilderness.

"How can we cook frog meat? We don't have any fire."

"Then I don't know; next time we need to have tinder in our bags," said Nan, feeling very disappointed that her experiment of cooking frog meat had met with resistance.

"Can't we get fire from fireflies?" Rob suddenly asked optimistically, because he saw sparks flying around as if they had wings. (Note 1)

"Let's try it," so they spent several minutes chasing fireflies, trying to use them to light one or two green twigs. "Calling them fireflies is really deceiving, they don't have any fire at all," said Nan, throwing away a gloomy insect in contempt, even though it was the brightest one, and it was still happily flitting up and down between the branches, entertaining this pair of naive experimenters.

(Note 1) The Wu dialect "游火蟲" (yóu huǒ chóng) probably refers to "萤火蟲" (yíng huǒ chóng). The sound of "但游火蟲" (dàn yóu huǒ chóng) is quite poetic, so this book decides to call them "游火蟲" (yóu huǒ chóng).
