The Issue of Selecting Athletes for the World Games: Shen Siliang Travels North Today to Confer with the Sports Community in North China

The World Games are scheduled to be held in Germany next year, and our country is actively preparing to select representatives to participate. In addition to Rong Qizhao, who took the Canadian Empress to Hong Kong on the morning of the 2nd of this month to discuss the selection and training of football and swimming with the authorities in South China, Shen Siliang, the general manager of the National Sports Field, is scheduled to travel north tonight to consult with the North China Sports Association on all matters. According to Shen's statement to reporters, regarding football, he will invite Guangdong, Hong Kong, North China, Malaya, and Shanghai to meet in Shanghai for several competitions to facilitate selection. For basketball, teams from North China, Nanjing, and Shanghai will compete in Shanghai. However, this is only the opinion of the Sports Association, and detailed measures will be decided after consultation. The issue of future training is also very important, and opinions will be sought this time to ensure that the players can fully develop with perfect methods and a good environment. He said he will stay in Beiping for four or five days. It is also learned that Rong Qizhao will return to Shanghai on the 19th of this month.

Jiangnan University Cross-Country Race: Guanghua Absent Due to Exams

Willing to Have a Friendly Match with Fudan

A letter from the Guanghua University Cross-Country Team states that the Jiangnan University Cross-Country Championship, originally scheduled for 2:30 PM on November 30th at Jinan University in Zhenru, was postponed due to rain to 2:30 PM on December 4th at the original location. However, our school only learned of this news on December 3rd, and the school is currently holding a mini-exam this week, so we requested a rescheduling to the end of this week. Jinan University agreed, but Fudan not only refused to reschedule but also moved the time forward to 12:00 PM on December 4th. Our team members have exams from 10:00 to 12:00 AM and 1:00 to 2:00 PM that morning, so they cannot participate. Our school has always opposed sacrificing studies for sports. We are afraid that the outside world will not understand the difficulties of our school's inability to participate, so we specially send this letter to inform you. Furthermore, our school sincerely wishes to invite the Fudan University Cross-Country Team to visit us for guidance during any holiday to compensate for this missed opportunity for joint practice. Guanghua University Cross-Country Team, December 4th.

Commercial News

Finance: Major Players Buying, Gold Price Continues to Rise Slightly, Although It Rose Midway, the Surface Seems Loose

Although foreign banks contracted in the gold market yesterday, the price of raw gold fell, and people's hearts could not be stirred up. The market was relatively weak in the morning. Major players took advantage of the low price to buy in succession, gradually pulling up the surface. Although the Indian silver market contracted, it was difficult to rise again. Early morning overseas silver market showed England contracting and the United States remaining flat. The price of the Montredier forward silver also fell by 5 cents to 3 cents. The exchange rate was slightly longer. London raw gold fell by 1.5 pence. The Central Bank's official exchange rate was announced, with England and the United States remaining flat, and the customs gold unit unchanged. The standard gold price was reduced to 1146.3 yuan. People's hearts were not stirred up, and the over-the-counter preparatory transaction opened at 44.45 yuan. Major players took advantage of the high price to supply, but lacked maintenance and continued to fall. The morning opened with a low, and it was still difficult to stir up. It was once weak, but because major players took advantage of the low price to act in concert, Mobil Oil still came to make the settlement and was easily pulled up. The official exchange rate of HSBC Bank was announced, with England and the United States remaining flat, and the market situation was hovering. The balance tax of silver was announced to fall by 25, although it lacked influence, the sellers took the opportunity to think about moving, and still slightly fell back. Major players still had the strength to buy, and the appetite of the banks was also fulfilled, and it was still easy to pull up. As a result, buying interest turned strong, and the floating space was contested to make up for it. The exchange rate gradually softened, and gradually rose. However, there was a lot of struggle in the middle because some people took advantage of the high price to sell. The situation has become stable. The prediction of Indian silver was a small two Anna, and the price rose even more at noon. The after-market closed stably. Grain　One Shipment of Foreign Barley Transacted　Long-Term Flour Plummets by Over 10 Cents

Yesterday in the flour market, both near-term and long-term prices plummeted severely. The extent of the decline and the briskness of transactions set astonishing records. It was reported that the previous day's ending had already seen a slight drop of 0.03 to 0.05 yuan due to rumors of cotton and wheat price manipulation. Yesterday, it was reported that the factories had indeed transacted one shipment of foreign barley (4,500 tons) at a price of 6.58 yuan. Considering the facts, this pricing is not surprising. However, the bulls reacted with panic and dismay to this news. Although domestic supply is insufficient, foreign supplies have begun to arrive, causing extreme panic. The initial price drop was only 0.01 yuan, but then the factories released supplies, and large outside bulls sold off their positions, temporarily going short and aggressively adding to their positions, resulting in a drop of 0.05 to 0.07 yuan compared to the previous day's close. However, the market took another sharp dive in the afternoon session as the factories continued to release supplies and large bulls sold even more aggressively. Long-term contracts experienced an even more violent decline due to the foreign barley situation. Contracts for March and April plummeted by a massive 0.11 to 0.12 yuan, the first such major blow since the flour market's sharp rise.

Oil Market　Shaoxing Firms Suddenly Try to Purchase Guide Sesame Oil

– Raw Materials Are Expensive… Price Opens at 19.8 Yuan –

The sesame oil market situation, because prices are high, is not easy to stimulate the sales of customer firms. Although Bengbu goods often see transactions of ten or eight dan, the Henan goods that have been quiet for a long time remain unmoved. Yesterday, the Shaoxing oil shops suddenly started to purchase, transacting one hundred loads of Guide goods, which is about 28 dan according to the Simaji scale. The gloss and aroma of this good are both excellent, and the price opened at 19.8 yuan. The motivation for Shaoxing firms to purchase is because the price of raw sesame seeds has been driven high by Western firms making large purchases. The cost of sesame seeds is not low, so the cost of extracting oil cannot be calculated, so there is a motivation to start purchasing sesame oil. It is said that this transaction is experimental in nature. Whether it is possible to continue purchasing in the future is unknown.

East red sugar was quoted at the original price, and East white sugar was quoted at 0.05 yuan. No. 8 spot goods were 21.65 yuan, and transshipment goods were 6.6 yuan. No. 9 was 21.45 yuan, and transshipment goods were 6.45 yuan. None of these were sold. However, No. 4 East white sugar for transshipment rose, with transactions at 6.9 yuan.

Blue and Red Broadcloth Also Rises… Western Satin Stabilizes

Shenbao Literary Weekly

A Brief Discussion on the "Hu Shi Style"

— Chen Ziyun

Some people advise Hu Shi to talk about politics, some advise him to talk about thought, and some advise him to talk about literature. Hu Shi cannot help but sigh and say:

"This is truly my crossroads"!

Mr. Hu, talking about politics is not your path, talking about thought is not your path. I still advise you to take the path of literature, and to narrow the scope a bit, to take the path of new poetry. But I am not hoping that you will still take the old path of "Collection of Attempts." A poem like "Ode to the Airplane" (see Li Bao "Yan Lin" "Miscellaneous Poems from Penglu," only the line "See the Guilin landscape," shares a character with mountain.) that kind of poem, seems to be able to be called a new path. The old path has not removed the traces of imitating old poetry, and is really like a foot that has been bound too tightly being released. The new path has only accepted the influence of old poetry, or rather has transformed from poetry, like a silkworm has become a moth. For example, the poem "Ode to the Airplane," its rhythm is like Xin Jiaxuan's short poem, but it does not seem to be intentionally imitated. Wen Yiduo's "Winter Night Review" says: "The rhythm of Ci and Qu is not entirely contraband in the realm of new poetry, but it must be subjected to a round of checking and sampling." These are convincing words.

I do not advise people to accept any "literary heritage," and even less will I pay homage to ancient literary books, claiming to be elegant and erudite. But if someone who likes old literature gets a good influence from it, and learns a useful technique, I will definitely not say that he "has the suspicion of reversing the car." Moreover, the new poetry movement is still far from the day of success, and the road to new poetry is definitely not just one, so it is okay to "reach the same goal by different routes." A "Hu Shi style" like "Ode to the Airplane" can undoubtedly be considered a path, just like the "Feng Yuxiang style" that I have mentioned before. As for the "satirical poems" and "folk song poems" that I have proposed (both can be found in Li Bao's "Yan Lin"), as well as the "peasant poems" (see Freedom Forum of the year before last) and "mass language poetry" (see Social Monthly) that I proposed before, even though no poets have left noble footprints, it is okay for someone to take them, even though the road has different sizes, widths, levels, and dangers.

Mr. Hu, do not say "there is a heart to advocate, but no creation." I very much hope that you will still bring out the spirit of a pioneer and create a kind of "Hu Shi style" in new poetry. This seems to be a path in your future, and it may as well be a path in the new poetry movement, one of many paths, even if it is a failure, you can also tell countless newcomers "this road does not work"!

Postscript: Someone told me that there is an essay on poetry in the third issue of Shenbao Literary Weekly that criticizes my opinion on the "Hu Shi style." Coincidentally, both the Literary Weekly and Li Bao (which contains my poetry) were borrowed by a friend, so I could not check them. I had no choice but to rely on my current limited understanding and first write this short article. November 20, 1935, written by lamp.

Streamlined

— TK

The Child's Heart

— Zang Kejia

It was truly something I could never have dreamed of – meeting an old classmate, Lao Li, from middle school in this foreign land thousands of miles away. I had no idea that my remote corner of the world was actually his hometown. We've been apart for almost ten years, counting back. Ten years is a large chapter in a person's life, so this unexpected encounter today is especially delightful. Although the world has changed completely during this long period, and we have each had remarkable and moving experiences, it's gratifying that we can still grasp a semblance of our former selves. As for looking a little older, that's inevitable.

Here, there are quite a few old classmates working; in fact, there are three of us who were in the same class. In addition, there's a Mr. ×, whom we used to call × Da Boy back in middle school. Time hasn't built barriers between us; after the initial surprise, the old routine of joking, teasing, and scolding reappeared. Lao Li is still Lao Li, × Da Boy is still × Da Boy, and I'm still me. It's a bit strange to think about: whose hand pulled us together from the ends of the earth, then separated us, only to reunite us here again?

To say there haven't been any changes would be false. Lao Li's child has already entered middle school. He came here this time to drop off the student – a child almost as old as we were in middle school, standing before us respectfully and innocently, reminding me of my own shy and self-satisfied demeanor when I was a child in front of my elders. This young child is already a husband! We teased Lao Li about this, joking that he had done something improper and was still so feudal, perhaps wanting to rush the creation of descendants to enjoy the blessing of five generations under one roof. We even joked that he would inevitably have his wife and daughter-in-law competing to have children.

The child listened to our jokes, seeming to understand but unable to interject a word.

"Lao Li, how old is your daughter-in-law?" someone asked, pressing him with another kind of smile.

"Um, um, I can't say for sure, but around nineteen, I think." His face flushed slightly.

"And the child?"

"The child is fourteen years old."

A round of applause and laughter followed. The child seemed a bit embarrassed and slipped away awkwardly. Lao Li entrusted the child to us before leaving, finally adding, "You must come to my home for a visit! It's only forty li away."

After Lao Li left, the child often came to my room. Although I didn't teach his classes, he was even more affectionate with me than with his actual teachers. His expression made my room seem like a warm home to him. The child was very quiet, with a light in his eyes that was as unfathomable as his father's. However, it didn't inspire fear but rather made people love him even more. As usual, he wouldn't initiate a conversation himself, fiddling with this and touching that.

A bit of warmth compelled me to ask him how he was doing, and eventually, I broached the subject of his shyness.

"When did you get married?"

"Last year."

"How old is your wife?"

"Twenty!" I almost burst out laughing. Children, after all, don't lie. After saying this, he became as shy as a girl.

"Why did you get married so early?"

"I don't know. It wasn't my dad's idea. My aunt told me to get married."

"Is she good to you?"

"..." His cheeks puffed up, but he couldn't get the words out.

I then asked who made his clothes and shoes, but he still couldn't say. So, I changed the topic. I asked him about the scenery around his village, his family's house, and the number of people in his household. This gave him a chance to speak. He said that the village was on the bank of the Grand Canal and that he often stood on the embankment to fish. He also said that his family had a small boat and could go out on the water whenever they wanted. "It's so much fun to steer a boat in the water!" he said, moving his hands as if they had already become oars. He said that the big flood this year had submerged over a hectare of their land, and they hadn't seen any of their crops. He also said that his mother had just given birth to a little brother last year, but he wasn't living with them. A nanny was taking care of him, but it was very close, and they could bring him over to play anytime. Finally, he described his house, drawing a diagram on the table with his small hands. He said he hoped we could come to his house and stay in the guest room. During the day, he would take us to play on the river embankment. He spoke animatedly, as if we were already on our way to his home.

It was another unexpected opportunity that one of my younger uncles came to study here as well. I quickly brought them together, which was very fitting. The children of classmates were both equally innocent and lovable, with the only difference being that my younger uncle was more lively and interesting. They immediately became inseparable. My younger uncle had arrived later and taught him everything with the attitude of an elder, but there was only affectionate help, without any arrogance. On Saturdays, he took him to all the famous sights here. Before they left, I gave them ten cents for candy (ten cents was a considerable sum in their eyes!). They came back in the afternoon, covered in dirt, and reported their travels and the expenditure of the ten cents, patting their small, black uniform cloth bags, which still jingled with copper coins.

Indeed, my room had become their warm home. After lunch or dinner, they invariably came by, and they always came as a pair. Although there wasn't much to say besides asking about their homework, seeing the two children leaning on the table looking so delightful was enough to bring comfort. At the same time, I thought that this room must also be giving them just as much comfort.

For the first few days, he kept saying that he wanted to go home on Saturday because the dean of students said that students could go home to get winter clothes that afternoon without asking for leave. He asked me when I would come to his house and also asked Teacher Yang when he would go. We all vaguely promised him that we would definitely go on Saturday.

Yesterday evening, when I returned after dinner, they were already sitting under the lamp. As soon as he saw me, he suddenly asked, "Teacher, what time will you get up tomorrow?"

"To go where?"

This question made my younger uncle very happy. He immediately clapped his hands and said triumphantly, "I said you wouldn't go! I said you wouldn't go!" My younger uncle meant that he didn't want either of us to leave because he would be too lonely.

My younger uncle was overjoyed by my words, but the other boy was utterly disappointed and couldn't say another word. After a while, he turned to my younger uncle and said, "You're going too!"

"No, no, I'm not going to your house!" My younger uncle's playful energy returned as he shook his head and waved his arms.

"How can you be so heartless! He invited you so nicely!..." As soon as he said those words, he regretted saying too much. It was clear that my younger uncle had only said those untrue words because time didn't allow it. If I could have taken back those two sentences, I would have, but as it was, those words had made the child feel a bit sour. I watched him turn and run to Teacher Yang's room. I could hear him from behind.

"Teacher Yang, when will you come to my house tomorrow?"

Teacher Yang also hesitated. "Um, um, I'm not feeling well, and the time is too short..."

"Teacher, please go! You can definitely come back the day after tomorrow if you leave tomorrow. What's so bad about asking for a few hours of leave?"

"I'm too busy with my studies, and I've only been here for a short time. It wouldn't be good to ask for leave just to have fun..."

He came back to my room for the second time. At that moment, my younger uncle had gone to another teacher's room. I saw that his small eyes were initially red under the lamplight. I looked away, not daring to look at him directly, for a moment, tears welled up in his eyes.

"Don't be sad. I'll talk to your Teacher Yang, and we'll definitely be able to go..."

The tears fell at those words.

I felt very bad myself. We had shattered a child's beautiful dream with just a few sentences! I brought him a basin of water and handed him a towel. He had just finished washing when my younger uncle burst in, asking, "×××, you're going by yourself tomorrow, right!" As he spoke, he smacked his lips. The other boy didn't say a word, just rubbing his eyes hard with both small hands.

Crows

— Yuan Chenying

—One of the Sketches from the Frontier—

Crows are considered inauspicious by people. Hu Shi seems to have a new poem about crows: "I wake up early in the morning, standing on the roof of someone's house, cawing, cawing. People dislike me, saying I am unlucky." People dislike crows precisely because they caw, because they are gossipy and don't stay in their place.

I once lived in the gentle Jiangnan south of the Yangtze, with its beautiful sunny days, after traveling from this desert frontier in the north. I even strolled along the West Lake. However, in those places, I felt weak all over, unable to exert any strength. So, I deeply missed the desolate land beyond the Great Wall, swept by the howling northwest wind. However, what I missed most was the vast, boundless, blue sky, filled with thousands upon thousands of crows flying and wailing at dusk. They seemed to be lamenting the fate of all humanity, in harmony with the sound of the wind, like millions of stampeding cattle passing through the poplar trees! Oh! How truly I missed the desolate frontier while in the peaceful south!

Now, I have returned. It is just the beginning of winter, and the wind, like a mad tiger, roars ferociously from behind the Daqing Mountains, blowing so hard that one's heart shivers with cold. Icy white snow has piled up again on the peaks of the melancholy Daqing Mountains; it is winter! People have put on heavy old sheepskin coats and thick felt shoes. On the streets and roads, there are only a few pedestrians, shrunken with cold. The wind carries sand, swirling into everyone's eyes. The withered poplar trees make a rustling, mournful sound. You might truly think: "Have I arrived in the uninhabited Arctic?"

However, what is still commendable is the crow, which is considered unlucky by people. I wake up in the morning. The wind is howling, and the world seems to be approaching the end of days. Only the cawing of crows on the old trees behind the house reminds you that you are still in a world of flesh and blood. However, after I get up, as the crows search for food in the wilderness, Guihua City becomes as silent as death.

Until evening, when the sunset in the west reflects on the roofs of people's homes, it is the time when "night birds return to their nests." Countless crows are scattered across the sky, forming long, large formations. Their shrill cawing, accompanied by the sound of the frontier's fierce wind, seems to possess a force—a force of life—and only then do you feel that you have returned to the human world.

Oh! Crows! Are you truly inauspicious things!

Miscellaneous Memories of Fleeing from Disaster

— Liu Ming

Fleeing from disaster is usually a miserable and painful experience, but I have tasted its sweetness. However, this was when I was very young, when I heard that government troops were attacking from the provincial capital and that the Tongzhi Society's forces couldn't hold them back. My family hastily fled to our relatives' home at dusk. In reality, our relatives' home was only two or three li away, so fleeing was almost the same as not fleeing at all. But in the end, we still fled. The reason was that they were cutting down large cypress trees there, and in front of the house, behind the house, beside the walls, and under the fences, there were many holes dug for the roots that could be used to hide from bullets. I only learned this later from the adults. However, at the time, in my eyes, they were just good places to play games with my little friends.

Farmers are generally very frugal and stingy, but when we arrived at our destination, my second grandfather—my grandfather's younger brother, who was a farmer—instructed the family to put out those good things that we were only allowed to eat during the New Year and festivals on the table illuminated by the vegetable oil lamp, such as preserved eggs and salted duck eggs. He sat beside us, accompanying us, and said with a somewhat apologetic expression:

"Eat a little as you please!... Why didn't you come earlier? We're killing two chickens today."

My grandfather, who was in a depressed mood, suddenly put down his bowl and chopsticks when he heard that the chickens had been killed for us to eat, and sighed deeply:

"In times of chaos and strife, even chickens and dogs suffer!"

"Well, it's better to eat them ourselves!... Are you still keeping any?"

My second grandfather smiled bitterly, answering in a somewhat self-deprecating manner. Then the two old men looked at each other, nodding their heads with queues in agreement.

Seeing the elders not eating in this unpleasant atmosphere, my mother and uncles were undoubtedly very restrained, but I was the happiest. Because at home, my mother was extremely strict about my dinner, and when she saw that I had eaten two bowls and was about to add another, she would take the spoon from my hand, pat me on the shoulder, and gently comfort me:

"Listen to Mom, eat one less bite at dinner, and you'll live to be ninety-nine!"

That night, my mother didn't make any such encouragements, perhaps understanding that hoping someone would live to be ninety-nine in these times was just a laughable matter? My second grandmother sat beside me, holding chopsticks and eating some vegetables with us. Seeing that my arms were too short and there were things I couldn't reach, she would often pick them up for me and pile them on top of my rice, saying with a forced smile:

"When you grow up, don't forget your second grandmother!"

It was as if this dinner had great significance.

That night, everyone slept on thick layers of straw spread on the ground, as if on a bed. The adults seemed to be unable to bear the hardship, but I, on the other hand, felt it was very interesting. At home, my younger brother had a habit of wetting the bed every night. Although my mother washed the blankets frequently and often aired the mats, it was never as warm and dry as it was here. Moreover, in order to be able to run out and hide easily upon hearing the sound of bullets, the front and back doors were kept wide open, allowing the cool night air of late autumn to freely enter, making the house naturally fresh and clean. At the same time, I could lean on my pillow before falling asleep, open my eyes, and watch the starry sky standing on the eaves, peeking at people.

Living in the same courtyard as my second grandfather was another family of relatives, who were of the same generation as my deceased great-grandfather. The youngest child in this family had me call him Great-Grandfather, which was something I was extremely unwilling to do. Moreover, almost the entire family smoked opium, and the house was always quiet, with only some sickly faces visible under the dim opium lamp, occasionally making the sound of inhaling smoke. When I was brought there to play, I never attracted their attention, just sullenly leaning on the adults, as if my hands and feet were tied. But this time fleeing from disaster was different. When my grandmother took me there the next morning, my hands were filled with smooth, shiny chestnuts, which would slip onto the floor with a clatter every time I moved, making me rush to catch this one and pick up that one. I was extremely happy to be put in such a predicament. My grandmother, eating a chestnut, declined, saying:

"That's enough, that's enough, aunt, keep them!"

Our young great-aunt, however, grabbed out many more, saying:

"Keep them? Keep them for outsiders to eat? In times like these!"

Behind the courtyard ran a white soil river, which only filled with water for a few days during the rainy season in summer. On ordinary days, it was completely dry, with sand and soil exposed, allowing the families on both banks to plant peanuts and wheat in the spring and autumn. My aunts and mother, during these days of fleeing disaster, felt suffocated and wanted to find some interesting things to do to relieve their anxious mood. Somehow, they learned the good news that Yaoshu's fiancée was digging peanuts in the sandy land on the other side of the river. Everyone agreed to secretly watch in the afternoon, and naturally, I was taken along too. Perhaps the future bride had hidden away. (To be continued)

Singing and Weeping

— Tang Tao

Singing and weeping is a common phenomenon in times of chaos. It was so at the end of the Qing dynasty, and it was so at the end of the Ming dynasty. During some events not long ago, we could still see telegrams, petitions, slogans, and posters. In short, we still had voices, and we still had tears. Even the Old Buddha, who claimed to be "undisturbed by gain or loss," cried a great deal.

This loud sound was once ridiculed by everyone, and I was one of those who ridiculed them. Why ridicule them? The reason is very simple: what I ridiculed was not the telegrams, petitions, slogans, and posters, but the people who sent, petitioned, shouted, and posted, who only knew how to send, petition, shout, and post, and had no other way, and no other positive actions. If they were shouting and posting while putting the slogans into practice, then I would still hope they would shout a few more times and post a few more posters.

In times of chaos, there must be some sound, and therefore, there is singing and weeping. However, those who only sing and weep, or only know how to sing and weep, should be satirized and ridiculed.

But since last year, we have gradually felt calm, and we haven't heard any sound. This is not because satire has succeeded. This nation has become accustomed. Its nerves are becoming increasingly numb, and it no longer has joy or anger, and it no longer has singing or weeping.

So, we are only silent, silent, silent.

Throwing down a huge stone, and not hearing a single echo; cutting off a piece of fat, and not shedding a single drop of blood. This is truly a strange desert!

However, what everyone hopes for is singing and weeping.

Since we can't find it in people today, let's copy a poem from the ancients. Gong Ding'an's poem says:

Having experienced all kinds of situations in famous places, it was never out of feeling for the common people.

After mourning in the west, celebrate in the east; singing and weeping for the former sages is more affectionate.

The predecessors were only like this, that's all. Common people, common people!

"Writing Essays"

— Cao Juren

In Mr. Zhou Zuoren's essay collection, "Bitter Tea Essays," there are several excellent essays on literature: "The Second Temple Fair," "Willows," and "Two Essays on Writing." In recent years, Mr. Zhou has advocated the "theory of the uselessness of literature," saying: "Literature is only to satisfy the author's expression of thoughts and feelings, and there is no other purpose. There is not much motivating power in it, nor is there any teaching. It can only bring people a little pleasure." He only acknowledges that bringing people a little pleasure can be considered a use. Since the expressivist school revered him as a master, these words seem to have become the classics for essays that focus on leisure.

Speaking of the usefulness or uselessness of essays, this is inherently in relation to the impact on society. If an author expresses their thoughts and feelings in words, but locks it in a cabinet, never allowing it to see the light of day, then the theory of the uselessness of essays holds true. However, that is not the case. Mr. Zhou himself published his "Bitter Tea Essays" in the arts and literature section of the Ta Kung Pao, allowing millions of people to see it. Not only that, but it was also printed in black ink on white paper and compiled into a book, published by Beixin Bookstore, allowing millions more to read and see it. This has social significance. Mr. Zhou's thoughts arouse resonant reactions in millions of people; the cry of a nightingale vibrates the heartstrings of a poet, who writes a nightingale song, which then vibrates the heartstrings of millions of people for millions of years. No one can erase the effect of this cry. The theory of the uselessness of essays can only say that writing essays does not come with the function of being a stepping stone to success, besides expressing one's thoughts and feelings; as for the role of essays in society, the author has no right to decide; whether it is useful or useless.

Mr. Zhou has said several times that he is from the Jiangnan naval forces and is an amateur when it comes to literature. But in his essay collection, the writing about writing essays is all accurate and practical. His essay, "My Experience Learning Chinese," has long become reading material for every young person. What is especially wonderful is that although he is touting the theory of the uselessness of essays, every one of the several essays on literature in "Bitter Tea Essays" shows the significance of the times. For example, "Willows" in the essays is precisely aimed at the retrograde movement of advocating reading the classics and reviving classical Chinese. He said:

"Students who specialize in classical Chinese in middle school cannot write essays. Writing classical Chinese (naturally, it's shoddy classical Chinese) is not difficult. You just need to first look at the topic, then find a style to match, and then write around the topic for a while, and you can succeed. But once you learn this, you become poisoned, and it is extremely difficult to quit. I usually don't give topics, and these students find it inconvenient, so I ask them to come up with their own, which are mostly large topics such as 'the rise and fall of the nation is the responsibility of every citizen,' and the essays are usually empty and broad. I advise them to change to smaller topics and try using vernacular Chinese, but after they write them, the authors themselves find it laughable, and the words and meanings are so childish, as if they were written by elementary school children. Ambitious students then decide to abandon everything they have learned and learn anew, starting from scratch to write ordinary essays, striving to use their own brains to think and writing in simple vernacular Chinese, while strictly preventing the revival and infiltration of shoddy classical Chinese ways of speaking and thinking. After working hard in this way, they can slowly recover. It can almost be said that it takes at least a year of hard work to purify the classical Chinese poison they have previously been infected with, and to re-learn the basics of essay writing. If they cannot do this, they can only continue to write shoddy classical essays, able to say empty words such as 'people's hearts are not as good as they used to be' or 'the land is vast and the resources are abundant,' but ultimately unable to express their own meaning. This means they are illiterate and cannot be saved."

When the quasi-old scholar teachers who teach students to read classical Chinese and write in classical Chinese see this passage, it is like having a bucket of cold water poured over their heads. Mr. Zhou's essays are accepted by young people, who know that to write coherent essays, they must follow this wide, flat road, and no one can deny his significance in society.

In fact, Mr. Zhou is always very clear-headed. He tells young people not to write those kinds of big topics, not to say empty words like "the rise and fall of the nation is the responsibility of every citizen," which is always earnest advice and prescribing the right medicine. He also criticizes Han Yu, saying: "I don't like Han Yu at all. His talent and essays are nothing special. He can be considered a model for scholars of all ages, but many things in China have been ruined by these scholars. They can only write essays and talk about the orthodoxy of thought, being vain, stubborn, and also ignorant and snobbish. Although they cannot become great traitors and cause great chaos, they are the most harmful in their petty meddling. As for Han Yu's writings, I can't understand his good points at all." ("The Second Temple Fair") This is also a kind of criticism. If everyone misunderstands Mr. Zhou's advocacy of "essays to satisfy the author's expression of thoughts and feelings," thinking that writing essays is only using a leisurely style to decorate elegance and pass the time, then they have fallen for the trick of the expressivist school's disciples.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Health and Medical Journal

New Methods for Treating Gonorrhea

— Physician Chen Peiji

Gonorrhea, commonly known as "white turbidity," is recognized as a difficult disease to treat. It is relatively manageable during the acute and subacute stages, but becomes more challenging in chronic cases, especially those of long duration. In the past, treatment for gonorrhea mainly involved administering urinary tract disinfectants and performing local antiseptic washes. These methods were often painful and yielded limited results. While internal medication and washes are still employed, the drugs used are far more advanced than before. Currently, the most highly regarded therapies among physicians are electrical treatments, particularly the latest turbidimeter for acute cases and shortwave diathermy for chronic gonorrhea, both of which are highly effective. The former uses light to kill bacteria, while the latter uses electric and thermal energy. Shortwave diathermy can be administered through clothing, making it particularly convenient. In terms of pharmaceutical treatments, the combination of mixed gonorrhea vaccine and dyes is highly recommended, one to penetrate the membrane and kill bacteria, and the other to stimulate auto-immunity. The effects are even better when used together. Among oral medications, Mesaltropin is particularly well-suited due to its strong bactericidal, antiseptic, analgesic, and anti-inflammatory properties. It is gentle on the stomach and intestines, and can restore inflamed areas of the urethral mucosa, making it highly favored by physicians. For local treatments, "Kolargol" is the safest option, as it can deeply penetrate the mucous membrane to effectively kill gonorrhea bacteria without harming the urethral mucosa. "Gono-Sorol," produced by the German Mann &amp; Vilz Pharmaceutical Factory, is also excellent. This drug is made from gonorrhea serum and Sorol, and based on the principle of auto-immunity, its efficacy is comparable to that of vaccines. It is particularly effective when the infection is confined to the urethra. My old friend Mr. Feng Shanliang, who runs the Chunzai Hospital at 66 Ningbo Road in the French Concession of this city, has conducted extensive research on the treatment of gonorrhea. The hospital employs several male and female physicians specializing in different fields, and is equipped with all necessary electrical therapeutic devices. Fees are reasonable, and services are excellent. (Mesaltropin and Gono-Sorol are both sold by Renshou Western Pharmacy at 1 Laodehang Lane, Mintiniyin Road, French Concession. The former costs one yuan per box, and the latter two yuan and fifty cents per box.)

The Effects of Opium and Morphine on Blood Vessels

— Physician She Lei

In animals severely poisoned by morphine, vasoparalysis occurs due to paralysis of the nerve origins of the blood vessels, leading to decreased vascular tension and lowered blood pressure. However, in humans, even medicinal doses can cause vasodilation, with the blood vessels of the skin being the first affected, followed by those of the face and brain, as these nerve centers are most susceptible. The resulting symptoms include a sensation of warmth, facial flushing, sweating, rashes, itching, and a slight increase in respiration and pulse. In larger doses, systemic vasodilation occurs, causing blood pressure to drop and facial redness to turn pale. The simultaneous dilation of brain and facial blood vessels is evidenced by increased respiration and pulse and cerebral congestion. Therefore, individuals prone to cerebral congestion should avoid morphine and opium preparations.

Treatment of Stomach Pain

— Physician Sun Zhiyao

The stomach is the main organ for digesting food and constantly secretes a digestive fluid containing hydrochloric acid, pepsin, enzymes, etc. Food entering the stomach mixes with this fluid, initiating a fermentation process that gradually digests the food. Gastric acid has antiseptic and bactericidal functions; it can kill bacteria mixed in with food. It also works with pepsin to transform beneficial substances in food into easily absorbed nutrients for the body. Gastric acid is extremely important for the human body and must be present in a certain amount. Too much or too little can cause disease, especially too much. The most common symptom of excessive stomach acid is stomach pain. While stomach pain can have other causes, it is most often due to excessive stomach acid. In addition to stomach pain, symptoms also include acid regurgitation, heartburn, and belching. Gastric acid has a strong irritant effect, and excessive acid can cause inflammation or ulcers due to excessive stimulation of the gastric mucosa, sometimes even leading to gastric bleeding. These issues are often overlooked in their early stages. The appropriate treatment for excessive stomach acid is to neutralize it. Discussion on the Treatment of Neurasthenia

— Physician Feng Shanliang

Neurasthenia can be said to be a common disease nowadays, especially among young people. This disease is divided into cerebral neurasthenia and sexual neurasthenia. The general common symptoms of cerebral neurasthenia are often heavy head, dizziness, poor memory, and insomnia. The general common symptoms of sexual neurasthenia are often spermatorrhea, seminal leakage, etc. There have been many articles on the treatment of this disease in newspapers. Although modern treatment methods have advanced and the general public's knowledge of medicine has increased, there has been no significant reduction in the progress of this disease. This is truly a deep social concern. In particular, sexual neurasthenia in young people is a local neurasthenic disease, not a severe cerebral neurasthenia systemic neurasthenic disease. It can also be said to be a disorder of the reproductive organs. Talks

The Usefulness of Firecrackers

— Jia Wei

According to reports, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance on behalf of the Liuyang County Firecracker Industry Association in Hunan, appealing for the abolition of the special firecracker tax. The letter from the Liuyang County Firecracker Industry Association stated four reasons for abolishing the special tax. After reading, I discovered that firecrackers actually have "unexpected uses," which was beyond my expectations. Now I am extracting it here:

...According to the Fujian Minbao, the Fujian Provincial Government meeting decided to increase the superstition special tax, including a firecracker item, and planned a tax rate of 30%... It has been found that firecrackers are by no means superstitious items. The former Hankou Firecracker Industry Association had previously presented the National Government's former Ministry of Health for chemical testing, and it was determined to be a sanitary product. This item is not only for the needs of weddings, funerals and sacrifices, but also to get rid of the smoke, making people feel clear-headed. It is truly beneficial to human health. It is a big mistake to call it a superstitious item...

Here, we will not care about (we can't care about) the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of poor farmers, industry and businessmen in Liuyang County who rely on this handicraft product for their livelihood, nor will we ask about the local ruling authorities' "arbitrary heavy taxes": however, from this, the huge use of firecrackers has been discovered, and it is felt that it is "unexpected"!

Generally speaking, what we know and can see is that in addition to "not only for the needs of weddings, funerals and sacrifices", when ordinary men and women want to worship heaven and thank the earth, and during the New Year and festivals, firecrackers are also indispensable. In addition, when the masses welcome a celebrity or important person to a wharf or station, and when there is good news in the war (like the night of the "January 28th" Shanghai battle last time), when a ball game wins, firecrackers are also used by one type of person. However, in addition to expressing respect and celebration, in today's society, which is full of grievances and widespread panic under the "economic depression", we can only "mistakenly" feel that these "yellow whips" and "skyrockets" are miserably and resentfully shouting "forced, forcing the poor, scared..." in the flying paper and sulfur atmosphere! And this deafening scream, this unpleasant stench, is said to "eliminate smoke and fog, make people feel clear-headed", and even that it is "very beneficial to human health". In this way, even if it is not "a big mistake", it feels a little "unsatisfactory"!

However, today, in this world, there are many things that can be "thought-provoking". However, when you find the "taste", it will make you "silently laugh". The appearance is really "impressive", but in fact, the inside is just a bag of straw - the so-called "gilded lilies" - it seems "plausible", but when broken, it is "nothing more than that". What watermelon seeds and peanuts are called "kings", and stinky tofu curds are indeed advertised as "hygienic"; students invented (?) "scientific altars"; fortune tellers can call themselves "philosophical masters"... even clown-like jokes are holding up the "humor" card; it is clearly an imperialist invasion, but they are taking "friendship", "promotion", "East Asian peace" and "instilling civilization" as a guise.

Originally, our society is generally performing many self-deceiving, profit-inducing, intimidating, etc. Jialin's tricks. Therefore, it is no coincidence that firecrackers, which have been proven by the Ministry of Health to be toxin-free and designated as "sanitary products", have become "medical products" and "stimulants" that are "very beneficial to human health".

Riguan Teahouse

— Yan

Small Records of Rural Travel

If outsiders come to our county seat and want to take a trip, the local leaders will definitely tell them without hesitation: the Confucius Temple outside the East Gate and the Riguan Teahouse outside the West Gate. The Confucius Temple is three miles outside the East Gate, and nearby is a cemetery. Among the overgrown weeds and solitary mounds, the Confucius Temple shows its dignity with its magnificent red walls under the setting sun. So even if there is no idol of Confucius, it can also be used as a picturesque scenic spot for visitors to linger. But it is puzzling that the Riguan Teahouse is listed as a famous site in the county alongside the Confucius Temple. It's a long story!

First: The Riguan Teahouse has been rebuilt into a Western-style house with a middle school after the fire. On the day of its reopening, it sold out for more than ten days because of the boast of the Western-style house. Whether in the same industry or in various transactions, it has always maintained the county's highest sales record. Until now, the Riguan Teahouse's business has always been dominant among its peers. Second: Believe it or not, the Riguan Teahouse is a three-story building! This is not because the residents of the county are short-sighted, what is so amazing about a three-story building? In fact, public institutions in the county, such as the county government, the Public Security Bureau, and even the richest tycoons in the county, such as the so-called millionaires Zhang, do not have houses exceeding two stories; isn't this the prestige of the Riguan Teahouse? The newly built three-story Western-style building!

Knowing this, then when you come to this city to travel, you must admire this three-story Riguan Teahouse. It is one of the two major scenic spots in the county, along with the Confucius Temple. There is also a history behind it!

Although I went to the Riguan Teahouse with my grandfather to eat sweets when I was five or six years old, and I still go there occasionally when I return to my hometown, I have heard this history countless times. But everyone has their own opinion, and since there is no county record to verify it, it is better to treat it as a myth. In short, in the Qing Dynasty, or even in the Ming Dynasty, an imperial envoy passed through this city, and he disguised himself and went to this teahouse to sip tea. When he sat until dusk, the golden light of the setting sun hanging on the city's walls shone brightly on the teahouse. Perhaps inspired by the Riguan Peak of Mount Tai, the imperial envoy thought that watching the sunrise from this teahouse would also be a beautiful scene, so he took out a pen from his bag and named it Riguan Teahouse. And he was inspired to write a poem, and then left. The next day, the gentry of the county knew about this, but the imperial envoy had already sailed away overnight. So they spent money to put the four characters "Riguan Teahouse" on a plaque, and the poem was also framed and hung above the plaque. I didn't pay attention to what the poem said when I was a child, and when I wanted to pay attention, the Riguan Teahouse suffered a fire. The plaque in the three-story Western-style house now is not the original.

The tea on the second floor of the Riguan Teahouse is divided into three prices. The bottom floor is for vendors and footmen to trade and rest, and a pot of fragrant tea costs ten cents. The second floor is where elementary school teachers and shop clerks and other shirt-wearing classes gather, and the price is doubled. The third floor can be called the mandarin jacket class. Although there are also fashionable young people in suits and leather shoes now, those who are not the top people in the county are not qualified to step on the third floor. The furnishings on the upper floor are also superior to all other teahouses: along the four walls are redwood kang beds, separated by tables, with seasonal flowers on the tables, and padded cushions in winter and straw mats in summer on the kang beds, so it is extremely comfortable to lie down and sip tea and chat. Even the central tea seats are red wooden tables with marble tops, and each table has four rattan chairs for playing small mahjong and playing Go. A pot of fragrant tea costs one dime, which is the highest price among the county's peers. If the imperial envoy could live a long life, he probably wouldn't have the mood to inscribe a name and write a poem if he revisited the teahouse today.

This time I traveled to the countryside for ten days, and because I was forced by public and private affairs, I couldn't find any free time to go to the Riguan Teahouse to admire the new scenery. My family told me that quarrels and fights often occur in the Riguan Teahouse (naturally referring to the third floor), because the teahouse waiter is scheming, and those tea customers want to play new tricks. At night, there are usually singing groups, Suzhou opera, and Ming opera and other roaming theater troupes performing new tricks there, which makes the gentlemen and young masters of the mandarin jacket class uneasy, and leads to disgraceful acts of quarreling and fighting.

I think that the reputation of the Riguan Teahouse may exceed that of the Confucius Temple with its towering walls. Perhaps there will be a day when the local leaders will tell outsiders that the county's only scenic spot is the Riguan Teahouse, that newly built three-story Western-style building.

Unemployment

— Wen

I was jolted awake by the alarm clock at eight o'clock. My secret wish from last night—to sleep soundly—ultimately failed because I'm not used to it. Subconsciously, I wound the alarm clock fully before going to bed. I craned my neck out from under the covers and glanced at the dim window, thinking of turning over and going back to sleep, but my wife brought in a basin of water. She gets up half an hour earlier than I do every day to prepare my breakfast. Hearing the alarm, she comes in to wake me. For years, she's been like a machine, never changing. But from today onward, I no longer need to get up at eight o'clock. I can sleep whenever I want. However, my wife doesn't know yet, and I'm unwilling to disrupt the order of the family with this unfortunate news, even though it will inevitably be exposed one day. I quickly got out of bed, washed up, ate breakfast, and left the house with my briefcase.

Outside the door, heavy fog hung in the air, like a stone weighing down my heart, making me lose my sense of direction. I stood at the entrance of the alley, debating with myself: Where should I go? And where could I stay for the whole day? I slowly walked to the tram stop and encountered a colleague from work—no, I should say a friend now. "Where are you going?" he asked me—a question I couldn't answer myself. At work, we had the best relationship, and he wouldn't make fun of me for losing my job, but I instinctively felt it was an arrow, insulting me. I glared at him, answering as if scolding a subordinate: "Hmph! There's no food to eat here; there are plenty of places to eat!" My friend didn't get angry; he gripped my hand tightly: "Congratulations! I'll come visit you in a day or two…" He jumped onto the tram that was pulling into the station and left.

Page 17

I felt a little relieved. I was glad I had that courage. But he's my friend. If it had been that foreign devil who yelled "Pig, get out!" yesterday, how much more self-satisfied I would be!

Tram after tram passed by, and the people at the station gradually thinned out. The newspaper boy looked at me strangely, wondering if he knew I had nowhere to go today. I still bought a newspaper from him. While he was peddling to others, I slipped away. I hurriedly walked a bit, and the thick fog had dissipated. I saw the standard clock on the post; it was already ten past nine. The question pressed me relentlessly again. If I encountered my friend again at this time, would I still have the courage to answer him that way? Thinking like this, I retreated into a quiet street, walking along the wall like a thief, with my head lowered, not daring to look ahead. I was afraid of seeing people's eyes! Passing the entrance of the park, I stopped. This was a free world, where I could stay for the whole day. So I turned in, found a quiet corner, faced the sun, and unfolded the newspaper to read. One page, two pages, three pages, four pages, supplements, advertisements—those advertisements had bloody words. I felt tired. I looked up at the sky. The sun wasn't overhead yet. Isn't just sitting here being foolish? Today this body should be a little free. The park has a very good early winter scene! I stood up and walked along the pond, like those gentlemen in leather coats, leaning on their canes, slowly, as if I were a painter or a poet, leisurely searching for materials for painting or poetry. I walked across the lawn, turned around the winding path, circled around the thatched pavilion, and returned to the pond again. Doing this once or twice, I felt like I was stuck in some kind of trap, with no way out. Looking at the shadow under my feet gradually shrinking, and feeling hungry, I came out and pushed open the glass door of a Russian restaurant.

The owner, with a big belly, welcomed me with a smile. Today he should be my confidant. His eyes weren't as fierce as other people's, squinting almost into a line. But wouldn't it be better if he had no eyes?

I ordered some strong Russian wine, ate a hearty meal, and was sent back to the quiet street. Then the problem of "the whole day" became "half a day," but even half a day takes half a day to pass. Time flies like an arrow. I suddenly recited this famous sentence I had learned since elementary school and laughed to myself, inexplicably.

Turning around three streets, I forgot if I had turned a corner, and how I arrived again at the entrance of the park. Naturally, I turned in again. At this time, there was no one in the park. I found the iron chair where I had sat in the morning and unfolded the newspaper to read again, sniffing through every telegram and news item like a newspaper editor. In the corner of the fifth page, I discovered a big secret: "A certain large and reputable insurance company is recruiting clerks and typists." I cursed "Pig, bastard!" How come I didn't see this secret when I flipped through the newspaper for half the morning? Excitedly, I cut out this secret with a small knife and hid it in my coat pocket. "Hmph! There's no food to eat here; there are plenty of places to eat!" Thinking this, I hoped my friend would come visit me tomorrow night. I threw the newspaper into the pond and walked out of the park, preparing to spend a few cents to see a movie at a small cinema. Today should be a little free!

I returned home at six o'clock, half an hour later than usual. My wife asked if I was busy at work? I didn't answer, holding the evening paper to block my face, silently reciting the address of the insurance company.

Singing the News

— Xinye

The autumn evenings in the countryside are lonely.

Occasionally, a gust of desolate autumn wind lightly climbs over the roof ridge, causing a few withered leaves in the tile crevices to roll and rustle.

After dinner, everyone, as usual, has to think of some entertainment to pass the long dusk; but tonight, that entertainment has become a problem. Everyone is anxiously wondering in their hearts, gathering around a kerosene lamp, talking about some boring trivialities. The dim yellow light shines on the gray, dim, and bare walls, painting many vague outlines of our shadows on the wall.

The surroundings are quiet and solemn. Even the squeaking sound of a mouse crawling on the roof beams can be heard very clearly—(To be continued)

Xia Hesheng, Three Smiles

Dunben (800) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening Piece "Scenic Spots of Three Wu"

Flourishing and serene, speaking of Suzhou. Outside the city, Tiger Hill is considered a scenic spot. Lingyan and Tianping are filled with ancient sites. It is said that Emperor Qianlong toured the south and also visited. The scenery of Shi Lake is originally like a painting. Not letting West Lake monopolize the beauty. Having just passed Mid-Autumn, going to Lengjia. The clear waves reflect the moon, rowing a small boat. Going west, the mountains and forests are deep and secluded. The misty clouds are endless. Hanshan and Shide left traces of immortals. Only for the sake of the secluded scenery of the Three Wu. Don't say that the western suburbs have many beautiful scenes. It's just that. The prosperity in the city is also unparalleled. Shops are lined up one after another. Selling all kinds of goods at any time. Seeing friends. Going to banquets. Coming and going incessantly like a river. With a clanging sound, they speed away. Dazzling new cars don't stop. In summer, silk garments are as thin as cicada wings. In cold weather, sable coats and fox furs are worn. Competing in new clothes. Walking down the street. Suddenly encountering each other, they pause and stare. The most difficult thing to obtain. Is the Wu people's naturally soft voices. Entering the ears, they can dispel ten thousand sorrows. How many lifetimes of cultivation to be in the land of Gusu. Living in this paradise is better than being a millionaire. Why bother to be busy as a horse or ox all day long.

Tongle Radio broadcasts the Water Margin's Lu Shi Hui by Yangzhou Pinghua (storytelling) artist Wang Shaotang every day from 10:00 PM to 11:00 PM. Wang Shaotang is the leading Pinghua artist in Yangzhou. His ability to spread far and wide is due to his unique and extraordinary skills. Those who love to listen to this art can all enjoy it. The wavelength of Tongle Radio is 720.

It is heard that Liu Yawei, a dramatist, is the person who has been broadcasting radio dramas on Foyin Radio every day recently. In addition to participating in the activities of the "哗哗" (Hua Hua) Small Theater, Mr. Liu is also a professor at the Shanghai Drama and Film Research Institute.

Movies

Guotai Presents "A Midsummer Night's Dream"

Inspection Committee Permits Public Screening, Movie Fans' Eyes Are Blessed

Warner Pictures, an authority in the American film industry, after more than two years of careful preparation and spending 1.5 million yuan of capital, exhausted the efforts of thousands of people, brought Shakespeare's great poetic drama "A Midsummer Night's Dream" to the screen. They also invited the world-renowned stage director Reinhardt to direct the film. He is the teacher of famous director Lubitsch and famous actor Emil Jannings. His artistic skill is highly admired. All the actors in the film were carefully selected by Reinhardt and were able to fulfill their roles satisfactorily. No wonder that after the film was completed, it caused a sensation when it was publicly screened in Europe and the United States.

When the film was shipped to China, the Inspection Committee was very cautious when passing the film because the content had bizarre and fantastical deities. The license issued to Warner for the screening of the film had an additional note attached, which read as follows: "The film 'A Midsummer Night's Dream' is based on a famous work by the great writer Shakespeare. It is now made into a film by Warner First National Pictures Company of America. It is humorous, magnificent, and can be called an excellent structure. Although the content of the plot is full of illusions and wonders, it cannot be compared with other supernatural films. In order to preserve the artistic value of the film, special permission is granted for its screening."

This film is scheduled to be presented at the Guotai Grand Theater starting tonight (Friday). Movie fans in Shanghai will finally see this great and unparalleled masterpiece, and their eyes are truly blessed. The picture shows the fairy king, fairy queen, fairies, and monsters in the film.

"The Dark Angel" Public Screening

"The Dark Angel" is a rare, touching, and romantic masterpiece produced by United Artists in recent years. The plot is based on a golden dream of three little angels, who later misunderstand each other and sacrifice themselves for each other after they grow up. The film is extremely sad and charming. Without the combined efforts of the three great artists, Fredric March, the silver screen genius of "Resurrection" and "Les Misérables," Merle Oberon, the beauty of "The Scarlet Pimpernel," and Herbert Marshall, the new co-star of Greta Garbo, "The Dark Angel" could not have achieved such a victory. However, the contribution of director Sidney Franklin (director of "Waterloo Bridge" and "Smilin' Through") cannot be ignored. Therefore, it goes without saying that this film will win the praise and admiration of the ladies of Shanghai and the romantics of the world. It is now publicly screened at the Nanjing Grand Theater. The picture shows the male and female protagonists.
